O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of medical knowledge together with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is despised in our region and is looked down upon everywhere, so is the science neglected and lost, and there remains nothing from it except for the little descriptions in old books that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is abandoned.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I should bring it back to life together with the arrangement of this treatise in the manner of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who undertakes it to ascend in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and the distribution and the moving and resting veins, and from where they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, Hippocrates says that a name with the name is much, and with work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Now we say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, should beware lest he fall into error and harm men; just as I have warned many times those who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut, that is, an abscess of scrofula or neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of the neck; for what blood flowed out, the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died inside three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it were taken out he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was an open wound; and the ignorant surgeon bound the break over the wound with strong linen, and did not leave the wound at all without some kind of ointment or dressing, and left it thus until the end; and he commanded that it should not be untied, and so it remained until the leg became entirely gangrened and the foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg; and when I loosened it, he felt at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But despite everything, the corruption had already been confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who opened a suppurating abscess that had become infected, and then it inflamed because of the wickedness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	When a carbuncle, insofar as it is pure of melancholic humour, does not need to be touched with iron unless it is in the place where everything that is corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is to say, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Why you should guard yourselves, so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through God's mercy you come to salvation and be praised; and leave frightening diseases to cause grievous sickness; and withdraw your arms from what makes you doubt, and have faith within yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galien says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care for a bad illness, unless you are called a foolish doctor."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterizations with fire and medical cauters, and it is the chapter ordered from head to foot; and about the forms of instruments, and the handles of a cauterizer, and all that which is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and bloodletting, and wounds, and the extraction of splinters, and similar things; and it is a chapter ordered in terms of forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to foot, and in terms of forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of help and harm in each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the remedy and its harm are the longest word and subtlest science and secret response; and many wise men spoke about this and agreed with it; and I am satisfied that their words were few because I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that universal remedy helps every condition where there is matter, except for two conditions: namely hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexion with matter, they disagreed and said that cautery is great help; and the others said the opposite: that cautery is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not cure a hot disease with heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite say that cautery makes great help in hot and dry diseases that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true at some time by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And anyway, one should not meddle with it except by someone who has tried it, and who knows through long practice the book of cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the cures and the speed of the remedy; as for other complexions, we have no fear of them, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the wise men gathered together and agreed on cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and harms no other member if its name be known.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from member to member spreading disease and bring grievous illness to the afflicted member; and perhaps even kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire for its intensity and due to the goodness of its substance does not cause such damage, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found these things through experiment and the long service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of my speech, because I do not wish to take away from you the secret which is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it casts out diseases of the body, just as the philosophers say in demonstrating; so receive them in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and chose attendants.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is convenient in all times, because the annoyances which come suddenly are put beneath by the help of the cauterization; and indeed if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization has no relapse; and they say so themselves. But it's not so as they believe, because cauterizations are only medicines that alter the complexion, and dry up the humors which cause the pain, and are more valuable than other medicines in their haste, virtue, and dominion of their work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease may come again according to the complexion of the patient and the place where the disease was located and its power; and the superfluities are gathered in him through the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in the place where there is a lot of superfluity and moisture, such as denser cauterizations for pain, and the like things. And that kind of pain does not return, but this [other type] does happen sometimes.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth after medicine has been tried, but their intentions are false. And cauterizations are the last resort of medicine because when we administer other kinds of cures in some disease and they do not work, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clearly understood that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizers made of gold were more poisonous than those made of iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the wounds caused by cauterization did not become putrid, but this is not true for I have tested it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and gold cauterizers are worth less than iron ones, as they themselves said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And nonetheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell whether it is hot by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down; and if you heat it too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there are many obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of this we use iron cauterizers that we have made more attractive to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordained this chapter from the beginning to end so that the view may be more easily found.
dou cautere olivaire	(Note: This appears to be a heading or title, rather than a sentence of text)
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is worth for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two which one makes by the cause of an illness that is called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend from the chief to the eyes, and to the ears, and because of a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and pain in the throat, and likewise for all illnesses that come from cold so as paralysis and sode and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicinal solution clarifying the head, either three or four times, according to what virtue and age and custom of the patient can bear; and then restore the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the scale; after that place the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two eyes; and let the iron (or metal instrument) come up to meet you, if it bleeds from within then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", whose shape is:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and make a descending and spreading motion with your hand, poch by poch, turning it around; then lift your hand suddenly, and reward yourself if you see the bone 1 small barley grain in size; and if you don't see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that take 1 small piece of linen, moisten it with water, and place soft cotton inside, and put it on the spot, and let it be for 3 days; then apply a warm poultice in butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed; after that treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said that when the wound stays open longer, it purges more; and therefore it brings relief.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should cauterize so long that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other one said that one should cauterize so long and so strongly that it burns down to the bone, just as wide as a thimble that women use in their sewing, so that the humors may be drained out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should cure and close it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And I think that both of these methods of cauterization are not entirely good for everyone, except in cases where there is a risk of death. And it seems to me that I should leave them alone; because the skin is weakened by the constant solutions of nature, as we see in other parts of the body; and similarly, when the patient's skin is weak by nature, and the first appearance of the cauterization is more salve and gentle for me, that's what I will follow from now on in order to ensure salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	It seems like our conversation has taken a turn towards medical texts.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When a chronic pain comes in the head and lasts long, the patient must use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and cleansing of the head with oils and plasters; and if one makes the fire cautery that we have spoken of before, it is useless.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take note if the patient's head is of a strong temperament and not too cold; then apply the cautery under that cautery, which we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards make the cautery above each horn of the head just to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery in the place which is called "vasselz"; and it is one spot where you put a blister; and hold your hand so that you do not see even up to the bone: the patient feels a much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of that later; and it is necessary that the cauterizers for the horns be finer than those with which one cauterizes the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	from the head's cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When a sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the disease is spread up to the eye, and the head has been cleansed by purging medicines, and all the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases have not helped: then he makes cauterizations in two ways, namely with medicated fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicated fire cauterization is that you take a stick of alder tree resin, remove the bark and recollect it into one pot as much as two sticks, then make an incision on the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can place the alder resin underneath the skin; and when it has been placed, tie and bind it well and let it be so for 12 hours; and then untie and remove the alder resin and leave the wound so for two or three days; then put on a poultice of cotton wool in butter until suppuration occurs.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the poultice, cure with ointment until it is healed; and if you see that you must do these things of any purging medications that I have written or concerning the treatment of purging medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cauterization is done in this manner. Heat the iron in such a way that it is the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a bell with a small quantity of pus; and in the middle there is a small appearance; and he places it on the painful area, and holds his hand and twists the fire lightly, so that half of the thickness of the flesh that was burned is charred; and lifts his hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and discharges an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Then he puts cotton in the shape of a string on it, and places it on the area for three days; then I put wetted cotton in butter, and then cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", all along the point, and be careful not to touch the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	the migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure the migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and see that the cauterization with medicine and iron beforehand did not help, then it is necessary for you to heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign on the painful area a line half an inch long, and withdraw your hand once, and be careful not to touch the artery and come just short of the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when eating, and the nerves do not get in the way so that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut or if there is great fear for the one who does it, and especially for one who is inexperienced and untrained; and leave the work half done; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it is written.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cauterization is not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize a different part of the head in the same way as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have spoken of or chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	The pain in the ears from colds.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain of cold, and there is work done with medicinal solutions and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then warm this cauterizer which is called "point", because of its shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply the cauterizer all around the diseased ear, or on both sides if the pain is in both, and back away a little from the root of the ear since you have marked its place; and put 10 cauterizers around each ear; after that cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is nothing other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illness; and do not make a cauterization on appearances that come from choler and spume of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture that moves from phlegm and purgings of head and gurgling, and it does not get better, then it is necessary that you cauterize the sick person with 3 cauterizers: one at the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third in the joint of the two lips; and put the cauterizer on the part that appears healthy, and make the cauterization in front of the ear's head a little under the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cauterizer so high up that the middle of the cure is burned; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the form of the cauterizer that we put before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the blade be a little thicker. After that, cure the place as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we said, and it does not benefit and the sick person does not have a fever, then make 4 cauterizers: 2 on the horns of the head, and 1 in the middle of the head, and 1 at the place called "vasselz" as we said before, and the last cauterizer above the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we said before.
de litargie	of lethargy (a state of physical or mental inactivity)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this disease it is necessary to give the sick person great quantities of years (a type of laxative) and purging pills that clear the brain. Then, rinse the head of the sick person thoroughly, and put on the occiput (back of the head) a mustard plaster written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cauterizer: do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is clean, then good; and if not, then make three cauterizations inside the head from descending just to the collarbone, with a space of two fingers between each cauterization, and cure it as the others, and if you see it swelling, and the patient is suffering, then make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more above the two horns, and cure it until it is clean; and the cautery that is called "olivare", just as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and of what we have said before; after wash the head of the patient, then make a cauterization inside the head and on each horn, and one behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then make four cauterizations above the spine of the back; and leave it until the most of the scab is burned, and lift your hand; after cure it until it is clean, and be the cautery that is called "olivare" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the section about the patient being great and suffering from strong medication first.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot take the treatment, make them gargle and chew to cleanse the brain often with good meat; after wash their head in water, and I would make one cauterization as we have said before, and one on the forehead, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, then make cauterizations as I said to that person who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and be the olive cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, then make one small cauterization in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and become thick phlegm, then make the cauterization of many cauterizations as we have said for that person who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what we have said before in the section. (This refers back to a previous part of the text that describes a treatment for melancholy)
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After wash the head of the patient; after make one bundle of linen well made, as a circle, and put it on his head; and the patient should be crossed over (i.e. laid down) and held tight in all parts; then present the liniment, and mix with old balm; and heat it gently so that the oil can be poured into it; after empty the circle inside his head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week for another good management, as long as he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you want to cauterize the head, do so by making more or less points at a time with the cautery. This manner of cauterizing moistens the brain just as much; and then apply damp cotton soaked in lard and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the disease (or affliction) of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the affliction of the eyes comes first, then begin and give to the patient something to drink that cleanses the head and warms it from all moistures, and make him sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, command him to look back at his head, and make a cauterization in the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of the affliction is in both eyes together, or in one if it is in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and be the cauterization long according to the width of the temple; and beware of corruption of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop the bleeding with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and in the incision how to stop the bleeding, so that once a cauterization is made or an artery is cut under the two bones behind, there is no need to do anything else.
dou cors des larmes	From the body of tears (or From the tear-filled body)
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from their eyes are old and accustomed, and sit on the eyelids or near the arteries that appear on the surface of the head; and one sees that it is cold, humid excesses, then he does the cauterization I mentioned at the beginning of this treatment: .i. cauterize in the head, and .ii. cauterizations above the two temples, and .ii. cauterizations behind the ears near the bones; and if more necessary, so cauterize sharply on the forehead all over one little cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From within the body of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit at all, then give him to drink three ounces of cockle shells after the king's head; and make a cauterization in the middle of the olive oil cauterize; and make two cauteries of the cauterize that is called "clavilis" above the eyebrows, one spot below the nose; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then apply the cauterization of this cautery which is called "olivare". whose form is:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that the two cauteries are to be done on the two hairs just as long as the hair is; and do not leave your hand there until the third part of the paper has been burned, in the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	two eyelashes that grow into the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At any time when the eyelashes turn into thorns and pierce the eye, and it is done by cauterizing in two ways: that is to say with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the fire cauterization commands the patient to leave the eyelashes as long and equal as they are; and if they pierce them at their origin, then he binds his eyes so that they do not move until they have grown out.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown out and are equal, then the patient puts a piece of linen on his eye; afterwards he marks on the paper the shape of the myrtle flower, and it is the beginning of the sign near the eyelashes; then he puts wet cotton in egg glue and muskailage of persimmon on the eye, then he heats the cauterizer to this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have marked with a dot and a small spot many times, so that the burn is scorched in that place. And the sign of the work's healthiness is when you see the paper shrink back, and the eyelashes raised to the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like that for three days, then put wet cotton in butter until the scorching has gone away. Afterwards cure with ointment until they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the eyelashes come back and the paper is softened, then start the cauterization again on the same place, just as you did at first; and if the lashes are longer, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and is equal, and does not pierce the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medicine cauterizer is that you command the patient to leave the eyelashes as long and equal as they are; then make parchment the shape of the myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot lard, each 3 parts, and grind them together well. Make it quickly, so that it doesn't cool down, then spread it on the shape that you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes. And if the disease is in only one eye, one should work on one, and if in both equally; and put cotton soaked in egg yolk under the eye; and the patient's eyelids should be clean and put your two fingers showing above the medicine, and press 1 part and let it melt every time the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, for they feel stinging as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then apply the medicine to the spot.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the inflammation has passed, then remove the hot pad and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted in the same way as it would be lifted by heat or incision; and if so, it is well. If not, put more medicine on the spot where the medicine hasn't worked, until your efforts are equal and you have gotten to the point; then put on a damp cotton pad in a burrow until the burned skin has cooled, after that cure the sore with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to take good care of your work with great care so that the medicine does not run out. And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair sticks in the eye, then resume applying the medicine on that spot which has softened like clean paper properly, just as you did before; after that cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the leaf of the myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to this, your contraindications; and do not think that you are on the right path for him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	It appears we've jumped from a medical text about applying ointment and treating burns to a new section of the text, which seems to be focused on treating fistulas (abnormal connections or passageways) with cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula, as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize according to this manner.

Command the patient to put his head in your hand; and take the servant's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor leave his head; after putting moistened cotton in an egg yolk or in persimmon juice on the eye; then heat the cautery which is thus: and shape it like the tip of a swallow's feather, together with the quill being the cautery; if you want, so that it is pointed from one end to the other, and if you want, so that it is also like a tent; but nonetheless, what is shaped is worth your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and drain out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and drain outside the bowels; after put on the hot cautery shape, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the eye above the eye, so that your hands do not go crazy; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be good. If not, then restart the cautery again once, and if necessary, and leave it for 3 days; after that put on moistened cotton in butter, and apply the dry ointment until it is healed, and if within 40 days it does not heal, then put on corrosive bitter medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king (the patient) according to how it would come in his booklet.

des crevaices en levres	cracks on lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Much of the time occur cracks in lips that are called "fissures", and similarly in children's lips.

de l’aposteme de la goule	of an aposteme (ulcer) on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an aposteme (ulcer) comes to the root of the throat or on the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and it has made putrefaction and boils and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you have a cauterizing iron according to the size of the fistula. Then burn out the mouth of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron reaches its full depth, and the last point; and do this once or twice, after which treat it as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it's good; and if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from the pain of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth ache, and you treat it with medicines and it does not help, then put the head of the sick person on your healthy one. Afterwards heat a cauterizing iron in this form: place the iron over the tooth like a cat on a mouse; and put the hot iron inside hastily, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and repeat the process according to your will. Afterwards fill the sick person's mouth with salty water, and let them rinse for an hour and a half.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was aching is made firm, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from cold or there is an abscess, and the treatments with medicine do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize in two ways: with a poultice (cautere de burre) and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautere de burre is done in this way: take butter from a cow and melt it on the end of an iron or copper spoon; then take some cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in the melted butter, and place it hastily over the aching tooth and hold until it cools down; and do this often enough until its virtues reach the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, then place them on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron next to it, so that the heat reaches the crown of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The cauterization with fire is done in this way: take a cat of iron or copper and make it thick so that the flame does not reach the mouth of the sick person. Then heat the cauterizer, and when its form comes out, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer cools down; do this often enough, because the pain will be gone that same day or the next. And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in the excitement of that cauterization, and then rinse with cold water; and this is the form of the cauterizer.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on whatever part of the head you want, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the bandage:
des scrophules	Of scrofulous swellings
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez. After which do another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and this is the cautery that is called "clavicle" from which we have the shape before us; and clean the wound as we said before until it is healed.
