And if you see the moisture abounding and the patient suffering, then have him do a cauter to the elbow, and one cauter on each armpit, and two small caters on the stomach near the large one, because the treatment is profitable when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, one or more, and are old and consist of cold and moist corrupted humors, and are cured if treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help, then do cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely under the lower part of the almacdate pouch and pointing in a triangular shape, and one cauterization below the mouth. twice;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that the stomach is chilled, and the food does not digest, and one sees the face swelling, then do to the face a large cauterization on the stomach, just as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with a sharp point; and leave the cauter over for a long time. After that cure the person as much as they are healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the flesh which is called "thelul", if you heat the cautery until it glows red-hot, and then place it on top of the "thelul" that has been cut; and I leave your hand there so that the cautery touches the birthplace of the vein, because the scab will form; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of "althelul", you should cauterize each one as we have said; after which, treat them with ointments that are beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the navel, it will cause greater pain.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the sick person cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, then comes this disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there comes a fistula, and it has become inflamed and discharges putrid and corrupted humors, you should try to find the root of the entire tentacle, and be sure to know how deep it is; afterwards heat the cautery until it glows red-hot, and insert it into the fistula according to the length that the tentacle has entered, and reheat the cautery as long as the putrid and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of the need; and be careful not to burn the nerve that lies nearby, and the large vessels. If the fistula extends into the bladder and intestine, you should beware of those places, and do nothing except in a safe area, and think that it is not possible; afterwards cure the place until it is healed, and if the place is sealed, and the materials are removed after a long time, then know that the place is entirely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is inflamed, and corrupted, and the bone will become like pus.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When a pain of coldness comes to the kidneys, and there is a large swelling, and no desire to urinate, then it is necessary that you apply a cautery on top of the kidneys from one side and also on the opposite side with the pointed cautery which we have spoken of before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in line, and this will make greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from coldness and moisture, so that the sick person retains urine, then you should apply a cautery in the area outside the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as your thumb; and you should do one cautery behind, or two if you need to. And the cauteries should be pointed, according to the form previously mentioned.
de la marris	of the uterus (or womb)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the menses are corrupted and delayed in their termination; and when they come, there is a great pain: then it is necessary to apply three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said for the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind; and the cauterizations should be pointed, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the groin (or inguinal region)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend to the swell of the groin, and because of this cause the hernia becomes dislocated from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and you find the swelling of the departed part: then it is necessary for you to cauterize the sick person on the swell of the groin with one cautery resembling a circle, and draw a line in front of the hernia around the swell as it turns, so that the swell is inside the circle; and let the cauteries be like those by which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not available to you, then make three large cauterizations on the olive-shaped swell, and let them be as deep as all the keys; and cure it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the groin (or inguinal region)
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the swell of the groin, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the sick person has been cured by what we have said in the section, but the cure does not last, and the disease is old: then it is necessary for you to purge the sick person of the thick, fetid humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, you do cauterization, and the method of cauterization is according to two methods: which are together burning medicines and fire cauterization. Fire cauterization is done in many ways, one of which is: that you cauterize on the swell of the groin three triangular cauterizations according to this shape, and I make a good depth and large, and there should be between each cauterization the thickness of an egg, and the cauterizers are olive-shaped. Sometimes we do a cauterization in the middle on the head of the groin, for which there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterization has reached the circular cautery that we have spoken of before in the section on hernia, but make it in such a way that the circle contains all the groin and all the fat of the key is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method that we do in sciatica, when the pain stays in the groin and does not reach as far as the thigh or knee. And if it reaches as far as the thigh and knee, then you make two cauterizations there where the sick person says that the pain lies to him, and one cautery three inches above the ankle, on the left side a little; and let the cauteries be like knives, and let the fat of the key be burned. And if the sick person feels that the pain extends as far as two or three inches from the heel or near the ankle, then cauterize there where he feels the pain three or four points with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then you do more of them; and if he knows that the pain lies below the knee towards the thigh, then you make a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and be very careful in all your cauterizations not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the sick person greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely inflamed, and the feet as well, and were pierced and corrupted all the toes. Afterwards, with a stomach purging from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And should be heated until it is entirely red and smells like sulphur; then place it on the hollow of the sick person's hip bone, and turn it so that the scorching side faces outwards; let the cautery burn once. i.e. one cautery repeat, and leave it three days; then make a poultice with butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure of ointment until they are healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use a pouch for this cautery out of fear of its gaze, and that whoever uses it will be seen; and nevertheless those are good cauterizers who can endure it, and the place where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or from percussion or from too great evacuation, or from appearance of spread cold matter, not one of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the sick person be rid of fetid pills or other similar things, and one make them on the back, where the pain lies, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the sick person can endure; and let the cauterization be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, do three cauterizations or four at the middle of the cautery with a middle nail according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight abdomen when they get sick, and fear; and you find this in the lower back and in the appearance that comes on top of the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, then cauterize at the cauterization of those (poins) according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If you apply a cauterizing fire to each part of the spine equally. And if you see that, cauterize around the spine with the cauterizing fire two lines or three, and let the points be close to one another. After cure the place so long as it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring cauterizing in a boil which is in the neighborhood of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is due to moisters that are spread throughout each member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which the physicians call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, so it is cured by cauterizing in this manner: make the mass of cauters around the jointure of the foot, and be the cauteries olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make a cauterize all over the spot which we call "point". And if the pains come just to the knee and at other joints, and they happen many times, then make a cauterize on each kneecap three cauters or four from each part, in all olive-shaped; and if you need more, then do more, but keep your hand back no longer than until the fat of the wound is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains come down to the knee and back, then administer the cauterize that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are at the hands, make points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains any pain in the shoulders, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ribs or to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and administer medicine. For if you do good governance and purge the bad humors, he will be cured with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rutting of the testicles
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling comes in the groin, and the intestines descend to the testicles and it is new, you should not cut into him that day; and he should use things which loosen the belly, so that the devil descends from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to tighten his stomach as long as the swelling remains repaired, and hold them at your shoulders, and sign over the incision under the swelling above the bone of the armpit, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which is its shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	As long as it is white and he vomits bile. Then hold the intestines in their place; and the attendants should tighten his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well on the legs of the patient, and put a cushion under him, and a sergeant above the thighs, and another above the chest which tightens his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold straight and steady as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again once more until you pierce to the bone; and take heed carefully so that the swelling does not burst when you make the cautery, lest you burn him, and thus the patient dies or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not pierce to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to their size, and of grown-ups also as large according to their measure; then after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the inflammation is removed; then cure him with other ointments until he is healed, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his swelling be allowed to remain for a long time, lest the swelling burst when he gets up to go to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, if a dressing is applied well made, and it remains for 40 more days; and have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of loud talking; and when you make this teaching, he will be entirely healed. And I will say later the cure to cut him in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, the same cautery of the cautery is repeated according to its quantity, and the third part of the cure is burned; after which it is cured according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized in the cautery at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the place of the incision and draw a line across it over the rupture, and another one underneath, and with your hands on either side fill in all the space with cauterized material. But the first cauterization is lighter and more shallow.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, from falling or being injured, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it must be cauterized with the cauterizer called "point", and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, its weakness, its virtue, and its location of torsions and pain. If it is cured by the first cauterization, that's fine; but if not, make another cauterization on top of that one, for it is customary that it should be moved to the member that is closest, why you must do the cauterizations until the diseased part is cured.
de meselerie	Wound care
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Wounds are helped by cauterization at some point with great benefit, and even the disease that comes from putrefaction of blood and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take note if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and there are no residues or leftovers, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the wound, then make five cauterizations on the head: one inside the head near the surface, and another towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the back of the neck; and leave your hand so that the cauterization comes up to the bone, and so that the scales come out if the vapors of thick humors can escape from them; and cauterize the scalp according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the wound is spread out everywhere and it's deteriorating visibly, then you should cauterize with those cauterizers we talked about on the head, and one cauterizer near the navel, and two on the spine of the neck, and five on the spine of the back, and one big one on the croup and another next to it, and two on the shoulders, and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the ribcage, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the backside of the cauterizer, because if you do, it will hurt. And at no time should you make a cauterizer on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that as much as I do of the cautery, more it does to help and benefit you; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in manners of iron. Afterward cure the spot with flour of times with honey and other cures until it be healed.
de enfleure	swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then the physician makes cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; and the cautery shall be a small point entering into the fat of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it be healed. And sometimes one does make a cautery on the hand and foot and back at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus is removed the swelling; and nevertheless, no one should interfere if he is not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves.
de albaras	boils or carbuncles (albaras is an archaic French word for this medical condition)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" (boils or carbuncles) is inflamed and medical remedies are of no use, then one cauterizes it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of fat on the skin, until the boil is removed and its color changes; then cure it with flour of times, lentils, and rose oil, and leaves of plantain, and honey from the beehive and almond sap, each one in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for syphilis (chancre) by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it is arrested, if you cauterize with a fire cautery that looks like .i. circle, all around the tour of the cancer. And nevertheless wise men said to do cautery also in the middle of the cancer; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it come to pass once; and a more direct thing is that it is cauterized around, with a cautery that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling which cannot be healed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When some person has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it delays from being healed because of the superfluity it makes or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is to say too old) and have pus in their blood, or because of the season; and you see it hastening to be healed: then cauterize around with many small cauteries that prick; afterwards leave it so. Because it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with which it is its shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced to the core, and be such cauteries that the sick person feels them throughout in such a way that the course of the ulcer is alleviated. Afterwards cure it until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than gangrene of a limb, for it eats away the limbs just like fire eats dry wood. If you see this disease in an area that can bear cautery with fire, then heat up small and large cauterizing irons according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize from all sides until you remove all corruption, so that nothing remains but what is sound. And then leave it for three days, and put on ointments over the cauterized areas suffering from scorching with oil until the burn marks are removed and all corruption. Afterwards cure it with salve-balm medicines engendering flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy skin does not appear, it is good; and if so, then re-do the cautery on what remains of the area corrupted.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the boils which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Boils often occur on the feet outdoors and are called "clos" by our intention, and it is a large blister that hurts the foot. And the sores of this disease are according to two manners. It's to say burning boil, and hot water boil. Burning boil is when you heat one cauterizer as sharp as an awl's point, and made of good iron to the size that it can pierce the boil from all sides, and that there be fine margins; after that put it very hot on the boil, and turn your hand completely around the boil until it reaches the bottom of the boil; and leave it so for three days until it starts to shed scabbing; then make an ointment with wild marjoram pounded with oil, and let the ointment stay all night on the boil, and the boil will fall off and be pulled out from its roots. Then cure the place with greasy ointment anointing so long as it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by outdoors the body, and many times happen in hands and on feet, it is necessary that you bring a hot water cauterizer; and it is in this manner: take a metal or iron canister, or an awl point, and put it on the boil and its surroundings, that is to say boils warts; and put the canister on so that it pierces all around, then add a bit of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edges of the canister come to the root of the boil, and let the hot water penetrate deeply up to the root; and suffer the patient a bit the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will be pulled out entirely from all its roots. In this way make another one after that, until you have extracted all those that are on the body, then cure the place with ointments that are greasy.
li cure dou trembler	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes with cold or heat, or quartan fever or another thing, you should make him four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the leg, and one on the stomach at the olivary cauterization; so let the shaker leave it and hasten will come the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	boils swellings
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At times appear on the body blisters or swellings, or boils, which come from thick corrupted matter. It is necessary at first when they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the boil: a subtle cauterization with a mulberry branch, where the tip has been grasped in the fire, or with the root of aristolochus longa, or with the lenticular cauterization. And at times when one has cauterized them from the beginning as above, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluity from which they come is broken down and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the vein is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Very often there are great hemorrhages of blood from the vein that is cut in the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when these things happen to someone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it as much as the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more gushes out; then heat up several small and large olive cauterizers until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery runs, and place the cauterizer on that vein which you hold your finger in, and keep the cauterizer there as long as the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauterizer has cooled, then take quickly another one of the cauterizers that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing these things one after the other as long as the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other malady comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped itself when the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cauterization, or by extraction if it has not been tied, or by tightly binding a thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and restrained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will remind them to stop the bleeding by tightly binding a cloth or by applying hot things on top, or other similar things, if they do not work well?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a surgeon or medicine present, then they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press it tightly so that the bleeding is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and they should not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water frequently until it is very cold so that the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make inquiries in advance for the things of which they will have need, such as cauterizers and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Il semble que nous sommes passés au deuxième livre des "Cures de Taille", qui est un ouvrage médical du Moyen Âge.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the sicknesses for which a fire cautery is commanded, or a hot medicine, and the reasons and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations; and I placed that chapter at the beginning up to this point, and I will proceed with this chapter by the same way so that what you want to find is easier.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus beginning with it, dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and because of this you must have greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and at the incision above the abscess, and in treating wounds, and in extracting splinters, and at the incision on the bone, and similar things; where there is danger and fear, and death comes to many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not undertake foolishly. For many kinds of people come to the cure, some who are so entwined with their sickness that they die easily because of the ignorance that they find in their disease, and from the great size of their malice; and these one must have fear of.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from those you receive their judgment, and they say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the disease is spiteful. It's not necessary that you agree to treat those who come to you with this manner, but rather put greater caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not operate foolishly but wisely on what you are certain of, and what you can take and lose; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients whose salvation may be turned; and that will help you to achieve good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter to you in sections, as I explained through the chapter on cauterizations, which I previously told you about from head to toe, so that you may find it easier to use what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the belly tightens too strongly on the child's head. And sometimes it comes from a cause not known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur in anyone other than children, and with all that I have seen it has been a hastening to death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is not worth working at these remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen a child in whom the bones were full of water, and the head was swelling every day so much that it could no longer be sustained; and he was so moistured that he seemed dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the eyebrow, between the brow and the bone; and the treatment is such that if the moisture is between the brow and the bone, and the apostem is small, you make a incision in the head as wide as two fingers, so long as the moisture flows; and look at the shape of the scull:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, as follows:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the corners of the head parted from each part, and when you press with your hand inside it makes a sharp sound, and this does not come back: then you must cut three incisions into the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture. After that, tighten the incisions with bandages and powders, and put in vinegar and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then loosen it, and heal the wound by tenting and anointing it, and let the head drain equally, and give dry food to the patient from pot of moisture as long as the member is comforted and cured.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you observe where the great distance of the abscess opens and the assembled sound; because sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess opens and the filling of the sound is gathered, and make an incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if you see blood flowing, so that the patient dies from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease that is called "catarre" in the eyes or at the breast, and the patient has been ill for some time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last resort is cauterization with those things which will sear the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then that you see the veins close, that the patient puts their head back; after you rub with a coarse cloth so much as the arteries appear, then pull out the patient's neck against the same cloth; then look where the other vein comes from, and the places of one and the other are behind the ears and both have been restored; then mark the places on the cheek, then cut one and the other with an acut knife to two parts as much as the size goes up to the bone, and that should be on the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the knife under the artery and cut above it, cutting also like two fingers across.

Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee. de l’estoupement des oreilles	It seems we have reached the end of the text. The title "de l'estoupement des oreilles" can be translated to English as "On Stopping up the Ears". This suggests that the text is discussing a medical procedure for treating ear problems, possibly related to infection or blockage.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through blockage of a wound, or a boil inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that it can no longer be seen; and sometimes there is one small hole with pus leaking out of the perforation, and the eye sees this clearly.

And it should be cut and scraped in front and behind the entire thickness, if it does not harm the ear; if the opacity is of boil or flesh of the ear, then take with fine tweezers, and scrape lightly, until that flesh is all removed.

And if the opacity is deep in the ear, then take one sharp scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or you take a plug and moisten it in red water, and powder with vitriol broth; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the plug and put another damp plug made of rose oil and wax, so that the swelling is removed; then care for it until it is healed.

And if the pus that has formed comes out, then plunge a sponge and drape it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the purulent discharge, such as treating with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the liquid that comes from papers of themselves when they are moist and dry, so you must stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and cut off the root of a spoonful of its roots; then put on vinegar broth.

And if not then peel off, so that he cauterizes with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is useless; and many times repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come from papers of themselves certain things that seem like hail in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of moist swellings above and below the paper; the operation is such: be careful if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know; then do the incision wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take with forceps, and cut. If you cannot cut without piercing a little the paper, it does not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble with a seam, and cure until she is healed; and if it's small, do nothing, for ointments restore her at once and bring back flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the paper, and take the granule with tweezers, and cut it and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pushed apart by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the granule is cut, pour salted vinegar into the ear, and cure the area with ointment that brings back flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyelids (possibly a condition known as meibomian gland disease)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Exinach is a fatty substance that forms layers on the surface of children's eyelids, and it affects all people, and causes great discomfort to their eyes. They come with catharrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces often and sleep on them, and have their papers (ie, their eyelids) moist below their eyelashes covered by the exinach that appears in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.

And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head in hot water; and then take one linen cloth, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained by the Exirnach of each part, then put it on him; and press at both sides so that the Exirnach be assembled inside the circle; then cut with a sharp instrument in a middle part of the skin a slit of length, and not be more large than the wound which is done to the vein; and make the skin in depth until you come to the Exirnach; and in more arrangements comes out the Exirnach from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces. Et if there are such men who burn thread and put it on to corrupt the moist part that remains, then let him cure until he is healed. des poilz des papieres	The hairs of paper.

de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that we've reached the end of a medieval medical text. The title "de la fistule de l'oil" can be translated to English as "about an abscess or boil on the eye". This type of text was common in medieval times, where healers and physicians would write down their remedies and treatments for various ailments.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon so call them "arissati" fistules: when you cure it with cautery and hot medicine according to what I said before, and it is not healed, then you make an incision on the abscess there where it should die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument that makes this form; and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron into one sharp point, and pointed like a file as in its present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is pressed; and do this as many times as necessary, then restore the area with drying medicine.

de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are born or appear various flesh tumors, on account of which some seem like scorpions at the end of their tail; and if it is one of those that has a tumor with rough color, and has a bone-colored tumor. In that one of these tumors which is soft and not hardened, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the oil on those tumors, and drive them out; then take what you can grasp with the sharp, subtle spatula from one part, until you know that the tumor is entirely gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be taken out, you should open it with all one of the sharp, subtle instruments lightly, until nothing remains; and if it swells or becomes an abscess, if the scab is cut off as it should be; and if it are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the scab is extinguished and all the tumors are taken out, then pour vinegar, oil, wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nostrils open and moistness comes just to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moistness does not pierce as it should, know that there is a tumor in the bone above, and the instrument cannot reach to cut it: then you must put one thread of linen, a little thick, and smooth with hands, and have between each node a space of one inch or less; and give the patient the ends of the thread in his nose as far as he can, and tie them so that they smell until they come through the nostrils into the mouth; and children often do this at school, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then take the end which comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end which comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know them apart as they are on the thread. Do this until you know that the nodes have corrupted the tumor, then pull the thread, wipe away the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back in the nostril as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the tumor; and then put a string on the nostrils for some days until they are healed, and if it needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nostril:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor. de la char sor le neis	de la char sur le nez (expression idiomatique)
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	A disease called "telul" often occurs on the head of the neck; it grows and becomes large over time, so noticeable to see. And if one delays cutting it out until it is large, take heed lest it be hard, of foul color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because that is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is clean in appearance, not of foul color, and you see that one can cut all around it, the patient will empty out and feel fear, and cure the place of scorching and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the swelling is cut and scraped away.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home some have abscesses in the lips that are hard like grains of wheat, small and large; then you must turn back your lips, and split each one open with a knife, and take out the pus and cut it up into each part; then put vinegar on the place after cutting it, so that the sore is stained; and then let the lip heal by itself, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper. des sordens	of the sores.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the gums, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and ugly scabs; and sometimes the teeth turn black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth stink; you should make the patient sit in your hands, and his breath be on your holy person, and pull out the teeth or scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and yellowness and greenish discoloration and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if you take out the first reason, it's good; if not, repeat the second day and the third, until you have everything extracted; and know that teeth need different forms of instruments to extract them, according to what the job shows, because the extractors who remove teeth from between the gums have different shapes than those who remove them from the head of the gum; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure the tooth of its pain, it's good to delay drawing it out as long as possible, because that should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance so that there is no excuse for pulling it out.
