dou retenement de l’urine	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the stone, or congealed blood, or bladder, or kidney, or similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to the stone being stuck at or in the neck of the bladder, then it's necessary for the patient to be bent over their knees; and they should have their feet on someone's back, and stretch out their abdomen from the part above the back, and restrain the patient as tightly as possible; and then the neck of the bladder is forced open by the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it doesn't come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it's necessary for you to administer an extraction with the instrument that is called "siringue", of which this is the shape: and it should be a slender, lightweight thread, like a bird's feather; and it should be about one and a half palm-length long, and fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of extracting the urine is that you take one thread, double it, and tie at the end a small pouch made of wool or cotton; then insert the threaded end into the syringe; and cut off any excess lacing and insert it right up to the head of the syringe. Then anoint the syringe with oil, beeswax, and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a chair, and prepare the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and aloe vera.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis so that it reaches the root of the penis. Then double the penis upwards towards the pubic bone. Next, push the syringe forward to the bladder and have the patient feel the urine coming close to the empty space. And this is not done in the above order unless the duct or tube through which it passes is twisted. Then take the thread with both laces and pull out the urine, then extract it and filter the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et c'est tout ! Merci pour cette conversation en ancien français !
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When purulent or bloody matter comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it distilled in sharp liquids and medicines, so make all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three holes: two from one side and one from the other, as you see it. The place that channels the medicine so that it blocks the penis well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and push when needed;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see that you are pouring your medicines into the bladder, put the top of the cup in the moisture channel, and draw out the drawing that is inside; if you draw out the moisture into the cup, and then push the drawing back in strongly; the moisture will go in and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheterizes the bladder: thus it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or gold, and the key is higher down; under has one fold or the strings come out; then take a lamb's bladder and put the moisture that you see to catheterize the bladder into it, then tie between the two folds with a good double thread, and heat one pot over this moisture on the fire; then insert the top of the catheter into the penis, then strain your hand onto the bladder all the moisture has gone in, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make one circle out of it, and punch a hole in the center roundly; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like one does with a door (dal), and put what you see of oil and moisture and water inside it, and tie it up as an instrument; and do so that you have done with the bladder, by pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	It seems like we've reached the end of this medical text excerpt. The text appears to be describing a medieval medical instrument called a "clistere" or catheter, which was used to drain fluids from the body.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone that is formed from rainwater, and all the signs, and which stone one must operate on by surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that water has jumped from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and I will explain further, and tell the patient to grasp his penis and try many times, and then relax; and there are many such jumps in the foundations; and is light the recovery of children until they have .iiii. years, and it is very grievous in old men, and happens most often in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is fitting first to cleanse the patient by means of a catheter, in order to draw out all the filth that is in his intestines. For it sometimes obstructs the pursuit of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the legs and lift him up and move him to the underside, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes protrudes from it. Then make him sit between your hands prepared, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then search for and touch the stone inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hurry now to cut on top of the stone. And if it doesn't fall at your touch from start to finish, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is old, or your middle finger if the patient is a young adult who has reached completion; and insert it into his fundament, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, then grasp the stone at the neck of the bladder. Then press down on your finger, and push the stone out towards the back where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand towards the top of the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the area where the incision is made. Then I insert the scalpel cutting, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make the incision between what is between the scrotum and the fundament, not in the middle but to the left of the anus. And it should be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be beside the fundament, and the incision should be from the side towards the back, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, but not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Perhaps the pressure on the finger in the fundament will cause it to jump out of its place. And be aware that there are stones with angles and margins: they are difficult to remove. And if it has those that are below, resembling a root, round and smooth, then the removal is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Make the size of the incision larger where there are angles and edges; and if it does not cut through, you must then use forceps similar to a file at the top to strain the stone so that it does not escape; or place beneath one subtle hook instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot tighten it in this way, then enlarge one small hole with a drill, and if the blood is poured out, then bind it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, then place the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut up above, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. And if it is very large, you must have to take it out through a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies or the urine comes out so that the place cannot heal; but nonetheless make every effort to draw it out, or to break up with forceps, as long as you can pull it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place on top one damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot aposteme; then lift up the patient onto his back, and do not untie the string until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, then the wound will have risen up very well with oil and water; then heal it with diaphenikon ointment and basilicon ointment, as long as it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if an aposteme appears in the wound and corrosion and clotting of blood in the bladder, and is retained by it, so that the urine cannot be passed with a sound: then press your thumb into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if there remains any, it will corrode the bladder and spoil it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then lift the wound with vinegar and ale and flaxseed, and aid him in every way you can, as long as he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the conduit of the penis and stuck there, and urine cannot come out; then I advise you to follow what I have said before, which is that you cut the stone many times, and do not exempt yourself from cutting for this cure. I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron instrument shaped like this, and with three angled points fixed into a stick:.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the iron instrument into the penis gently, as far as it reaches to the stone; and turn the instrument at your hand in a poking motion, back and forth, until you can pierce the stone from another side; if urine comes out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis. If it is thus broken, it will come out with the urine right away, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of something that prevents it, then tie one thread around the stone and another above it; next twist the penis between the two threads, right at the stone, and then pull it out. Release the thread, and clean out the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	This appears to be a new section of text, unrelated to the previous conversation.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the stone is formed in women, and it happens any time, then the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is pregnant.

And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of midwifery; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper inside than the stone of the man, for which reason it requires a more profound cut, and there is great fear.

de hernie carnouse	Il semble que vous voulez discuter d'un texte médical anciennement écrit, probablement en moyen français. Je vais faire de mon mieux pour comprendre et répondre à vos questions.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The assembled moisture or white secretion, which is under the shell of the egg, that contains the yolk; and it's called "syfac", and sometimes it's properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it might be another egg; and this is the skin of the eggshell between the white syfac that we said; and this can only occur.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this moisture is so weak that it comes to the eggs, and spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from blows above the eggs, and this moisture is of many colors: or it's colored declining to yellow, or it's without red, or black, or transparent white, and so forth.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and this is the sign to know this assembly, for if it is in white syfac that we said, then it is the reabsorbent tumor, i.e. a long sac like the figure of an egg, and does not open the eggs, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper membrane, then it is the reabsorbent tumor with part of the yolk, and because of this one thinks that it's another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the egg and the white syfac, then it smells very well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try to prick all around the transparent quarter, in order to see its form beforehand.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the pricking, judge of that which is inside. (This sentence seems to be a conclusion or a summary, indicating that one should examine the result of the pricking in order to understand the contents of the egg.)
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cut it with a knife, it is necessary that the sick (egg) be healed according to its power and the filling of its body. Then they place a wooden beam above it on something quite high, and put underneath it much cloth.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then have the patient sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two corners of the kidney.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula left and cut the skin of the kidneys among their length up to the point of the finger, and make the incision entirely straight cutting through the skin of the kidneys just so far as white fabric, and carefully scrape off the membranes according to one's power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the white fabric with an awl to one large perforation, and draw out all the fluid, and then put in your fingers, and hold the white fabric above; and do not touch the kidney itself, but only the fabric, cut away all or in pieces likewise the costal part of it carefully, lest if you do not cut it well and properly, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the blood spurts forth to your work, clean it up in its place as soon as you have completed the work of the membrane; then sew together the two leaves of the kidney with a suture, and close it like other wounds, until it is healed.

And if you find the blood corrupted by another disease, it is fitting that you tie the vessels that are suspended, by closing off the hemorrhaging of blood; then cut the kidney away from all the suspensory parts, and extract the blood, and treat it as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	It seems we've reached the end of the text! The translation is:
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this reed there is fear for many dispositions, by which it seems to me that one should not cut it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the signs of the aposteme.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many apostemes come in the body, and indeed in the groin; and it is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by superfluity of bitter and sharp humour that is spread to the groin, or from striking.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the colour of the aposteme according to the colour of the body; and does not find pain, and is a grievous aposteme.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance is a grievous aposteme foul and pustular, and of changing colour, and sometimes comes from no artery, or from the inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from no artery, it is known by the disposition of hot aposteme, when you press it to your fist.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and does not agree that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made from the inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fist.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well make an incision over this appearance and over the other signs.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you cut the kernel of the groin, then the swelling goes up, and the thread of the white scar tissue, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the eye is already sore with these sparks, then you must draw out the eye, and the cup.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is inflamed in the scrotum, or in what is inside the vessels, then you must let out all that swelling, and the cup afterwards.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the child is behind its place, then you must cup it all, and draw out the eye, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping resembling a bag, with softening of the groin.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the sick person groans grievously when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure for this disease is very close to being just as perilous as the one before.

puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then he cuts them in the middle straight on, according to the length of the body, and extracts the corrupted moors.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as with others where a boil forms, so that no vessel nearby nourishes one of the groin.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because through them there comes no evil, and if all vessels come with pus, it is necessary to drain the groin of all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the twisting of the joint
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this entanglement are due to the tear that occurs in the joint, or the stretching above the abdomen in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from this dislocation to one of the testicles.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this dislocation is either in the joint or a stretching of it, and these two manners come from different causes: either by striking, or by jumping, or by braying, or by lifting a heavy weight, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is a stretching of the joint, are that there occurs a "poc" and "poc", in a long time, and do not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the swelling is equal all the way up to the inside, because the joint presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a tearing of the joint, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the swelling appears in different forms, just under the skin nearby, and this is because of the exit of the intestine and the body's flesh from the joint.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the joints, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with vinegar, why it is necessary to be careful not to get burned.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the treatment is that you order the patient to bring the intestine back into its place inside the wound, if it can be put in.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then have it supported on his neck with your hands, and lift up the thighs.

puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle or a thick thread made of ten threads, and sew it into the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the groin; then trim the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the syfac, about which we have said that is under the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of two parts.

et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the rest according to the round shape that it (the syfac) carries; then trim in the part which is under the skin of the groin, as much as it seems necessary, and bind it up, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then moisten wool in oil, and put on the wound, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white scar tissue is cauterized that we have said to do after incision, by doubt of bleeding from the wound.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this has happened many times and leaves the ligament so that it can hang loose itself; and if it does not fall quickly, then heat water should be applied, and put on what we have said, until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone dare to do the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is done in such a way as the vines are intertwined with the beam, in the same manner as you tie the vases, after cutting them slightly above and below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then sew it together, and treat the abscess with what overflows, until the vases break open; and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes from the entrails, as we have said, and opens the hole; and no intestine should come out through the cut, and if one does come out, it's bad, and repair every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and always if it remains too long in that point, the wound or stitch will break, until the intestine comes out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the stretching of the stitch that is at the entrails, as we have said, since it becomes stretched, then softens and inflames the hole and opens it.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cauterizing, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and that the sick person lies on his back between your hands, then cut the hole of the inflamed rupture open wide according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pull out the stitch that is under the skin and sew what follows, then take the thread and put it on top of the visible hole of the stitch.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press firmly against the belly, then sew up the two visible holes of the stitch on top of the thread, and sew one and the other together.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull out the thread, and do not cut the stitch nor stretch the gut or any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestine vine.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with the treatment for wounds. And when you cut the threads, if the wound is unhealed and you still have to treat the wound, then do so until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The stitch is constricted and does not show in the rupture, and the cauterizing is more effective in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the intestines becomes softened in some people, because the contents inside are softened, and it can be seen; and when one wants to treat it, one must have the sick person lie on their back, and cut off the softened skin above the natural skin. Then sew together the two lips at a seam, and if you want, sew first the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread hang loose.
dou chastrement	of punishment (or possibly "discipline")
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Be aware that punishment is allowed in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to discuss it in this book. However, it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the barber needs to know how to respond when asked about the treatment of a wound, and the other is that we often need to punish certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
des hermofrodites	The hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphroditism is in two manners like men: one is that between the two testicles it also opens as the shape of a woman's figure, or it has hair, and sometimes in its court it urinates.  And the other manner is in women, and it has on top of the vulva also a penis and two testicles.  And the cure for man and woman is that you bind the swollen parts tightly, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, men from whom urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, have no cure.
de la tentigene	of witchcraft
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a swollen part on the natural body, as ugly to see as it may be; and some women have it just as big as a hand, and that's the treatment. You must paint the superfluity of the tentigene onto your hand or fingers, and tie it lightly; and don't go too deep in, lest hemorrhaging comes from it, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed; and there is another lump that grows on the edge of the vagina, and you apply it, and by chance it bursts forth, and resembles the shape of a cow, and for this reason they called it in the past "cow disease". You must tie it, just as we have said about the tentigene, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	It seems you're quoting from an old medical text, likely from medieval Europe.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When the natural state of a woman is not perceived, or if the vulva is small; and it is natural by birth, or caused by illness that has arrived; or it is due to fatty flesh, or dense, subtle, or thick tissue, and is formed in front, sides, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly having periods; and the knowledge of this is by the examination of the belly. If the swelling is apparent, you should check with your doctor or a midwife. If it is dense, subtle tissue, and it is close to the two lips, hurry and rinse inside: put your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then the two lips are formed, so that the subtle tissue is rinsed out, and the swelling is removed; then take some linen, moisten it in oil, and place it over the area, and support the woman at home every day, so that she cannot walk. And if the tissue is hard and thick, you should make a poultice like an oak leaf. If the swelling is due to dead flesh, suspend the area with the onion and cover it; and have blood-stopping medicines, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, frankincense, and an eggshell full of flour; then apply a bandage made of cloth, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus for a long time, and apply a linen tent to dry out the area; then be cured with other remedies until it is healed. And when dead flesh comes in the womb, you must cover it in this manner, unless it is an enchanted abscess. For at an enchanted abscess in the womb, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Voici une traduction de la partie du texte qui parle des émorrhoides :
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which, without cutting, commonly occur; and when hemorrhoids are old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive a cure.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the armpit
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many ways an abscess can form in the armpit, such as a carbuncle and pus-filled abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to tell you about the hot abscess that forms in the armpit, which is not one of those that cools down; and if you want to know how to work with iron, see if the abscess is swollen at the beginning of its onset, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it. Then do not rush to lance it, but let it subside as much as the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on one chair, and have two small stools where he leans forward, and support his back and bring his legs close together; and spread his knees apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then suck out the pus towards the right side, and introduce the instrument from which the mouth of the armpit comes, by means of which this form appears; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain; and it is necessary to put the spout of the instrument above, and to tighten the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is made soft by hand, it is necessary to cover the top, at the left edge of the scapula; and when the tube is empty, it is necessary to put moist pads in olive oil or in green oil into the wound; and place the pad over the wound at the bottom of the armpit, and on top of the armpit and on the elbow a clean moistened linen cloth, then cure with ointment for two days according to what we mentioned in the division. And if the wound is reopened in the armpit, it is necessary to take care not to work with iron again, but cure as we said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Il semble que vous ayez demandé un texte médical ancien qui traite de la gynécologie et de la obstétrique. Le texte que j'ai traduit précédemment était probablement une section sur les affections de la peau, mais maintenant vous me demandez de traiter du sujet plus spécifique de l'enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the woman to know the figure of natural birth, and the signs that are when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell the armpit; then the child hastens to issue forth in force; then you should know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the head comes out first, and the shoulders with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it descends over its head, then the shoulders come out with it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes out between her legs, or above the hips, or the arms, or on her stomach, or side, and becomes converted by chance over its neck, and by other bad figures; then it is necessary for the woman to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out over its head in a natural birth, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtue of her is weak, let her sit on a chair, or women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the ball (or dough?) between her lips, in the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	It seems that the text is a medieval medical manual, possibly written by a midwife or a physician. Here's my translation and interpretation of the remaining text:
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the exit of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out onto its feet, it is to be pushed upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it a little by little until it is straight;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and extend it a little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When he jumps as high as his knees, if it commands to bend, and makes him sneeze with condensation;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he jumps up, as God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump up as we have said, then turn it a little by little until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For at that time it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if he does not come up as we have said, take mustard, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and pound everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the natural condition of a woman inside and outside with this unguent,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in hot water until under the armpits.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, make her a belt of myrrh and put it under, and let her stay for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and compress her mouth and nose, and take hold of the belly lightly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the exit of a child from its thigh (or legs).
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the baby comes in this form, it places its feet one after another.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	Then be swollen on its neck, and have the legs hanging down, and be inclined over it (the bed).
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands one after another, and then take the hands to the stomach, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is (fully) arranged downwards.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the baby does not jump, take its feet and move them in shape, then move the stomach up, then put your hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and hold the baby one after another; and command the woman to take herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the exit of the child which comes out with a hand on the side.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to pull back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot pull it back, then make the woman lift and go (up).
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot lift up, then have her lie on the bed, and straighten out the legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then give the cord that I told you about.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not deliver, then have her sit on a stool, and try to pull back the hand again.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and hold the child in accordance with its natural shape, and have her breathe deeply, and command her to take herself until the child comes out strong.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of a child on its neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	You should have the bail hold its hand, then turn it slowly and gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, so place on the natural muscle of the elbow and oil, as we have said, then command her to move slowly.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, so make her sit on a i.e. seat, and command her to hold it; and then make her straighten.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by the same method for both wrists.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this manner to all the wrists, so bend the wrist at your finger, as long as the tendons are empty;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can be on its face and neck, so bend it from the mouth, that it is not held, and break the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have put it so that it fits, and command the woman to hold onto one time:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins (this text seems to be a medieval medical manual, specifically discussing methods for delivering babies in a somewhat gruesome manner)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at once; and this is not an uncommon thing, it happens often enough.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Double births are a strange occurrence, and they do not live if they have no names;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are torn apart by the placenta that divides them, which is attached to the mouth (of the womb).
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally just like we all do, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out difficultly, then do the treatment as we have said, and be subtle with the belly, and make her do quickly and easily what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is worth for the salvation. (i.e. take steps to ensure the mother's health and safety)
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb: one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more, up to fifteen, and they are all perfectly formed as an infant by the measure of God's glory.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is fitting that the belly knows everything that happens, for perhaps such a thing has happened to her as well.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do what needs to be done.
de l’enfant mort	of the stillborn child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead or stillborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to do manual labor;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is fitting that you know whether the woman is of good virtue and health, and if she has had an accident or fears death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is fitting that the woman be supine on her back and have her hands inclined downwards and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife tie a thread of two parts around her [the woman's] waist, or bind it to the bed so that she is not moved during the delivery of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then you should rub the mouth of the womb with oily moisture made from muskellunge of alea and fenugreek and flaxseed oil, and then grease the midwife's hands with these oils and medicaments.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then insert them into the womb lightly, then leave one loose or tie the ligatures that are suitable for that.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and be on guard if the baby is preparing to descend upon its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	and tie the ligatures in their own or in its neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the sides.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, then tie or pin it and take care of the hands different.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is fitting that you tie the ligature to her right hand, and put the handle between her left hand's shoulders, and bind all her hands lightly, and tie the ligature in one of those places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing. (i.e. until the afterbirth is expelled)
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the ligature:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then tie it against another ligature, or a third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal. (i.e. to ensure that both hands and/or other parts of the body are tied with an equal amount of string)
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them equally by moving from one side to the other, so that they come out, and the ligatures are pulled apart to hold them, just as this is the form: (i.e. a diagram of how the ligatures should be tied and stretched)
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then the midwife should anoint some of her shoulders with oil and tie them in that part, and treat the other part. (i.e. to help loosen any remaining tissue or placenta)
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains nothing, then the midwife should put this ligature or more high in that place, and do so until it comes out completely. (i.e. to ensure a clean and complete delivery)
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and you cannot return it for the binding, (i.e. because one hand has already been tied up)
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	it is fitting that you wrap him on a cloth, as much as it comes out, (i.e. to tie up the umbilical cord and any remaining placenta)
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then tie it up at the junction of the plant or at the navel, and thus it is fitting that you do so in the other hand, and bind both feet. (i.e. to secure the umbilical cord and prevent any bleeding)
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's hands are large and it is narrow in the delivery, or it has a sharp head assembled, (i.e. if the baby's hand is large or its head is misshapen)
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	it is fitting that you tie the spine-like spatula between your shoulders, and make the head and extract the sharpness; (i.e. to use a type of clamp or tongs to grasp and deliver the baby's hand)
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can turn it onto the instrument that is called "almidach", of which the form comes with the instruments or chapister that follows this one. (i.e. a type of forceps or pincers used to grasp and deliver the baby's hand)
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus do the same if the child has a large head naturally, (i.e. if the baby's head is unusually large or misshapen, requiring special care and attention)
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with forceps; (i.e. to carefully remove any excess bone or tissue from the birth)
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the hands jump out and are tied to the throat, and they are split, until the membranes that are in the navel come out. (i.e. to carefully attend to any complications or difficulties during birth)
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then tie it in pieces as much as you can; (i.e. to make multiple ligatures to try and deliver the baby or placenta)
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, it is fitting that you make holes until the membranes flow; (i.e. to carefully puncture any areas where there may be swelling or fluid accumulation)
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the baby is on its feet, and the descent is easy, and the approach to the mouth of the womb is light; (i.e. an indication that delivery is imminent and may proceed normally)
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrow at the belly or navel, it is fitting that you pull it out on a cloth wrapped around your hand; (i.e. to carefully deliver the baby by holding onto the umbilical cord and using the cloth as a makeshift "birth sack")
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or navel, until the membranes that are inside come out. (i.e. to perform a type of episiotomy or incision in the birth canal)
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if another member is removed and the hand remains, (i.e. one part of the baby's body has been delivered, but not the other)
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	so bind the midwife's hand with thread around her back and pull it just to the mouth of the womb. (i.e. to secure the midwife's hand in place and prevent any complications)
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then tie one ligature or two, and pull it out; (i.e. to carefully deliver the remaining part of the baby's body by tying a ligature around it and pulling it out)
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is tightened by hot heat that has come to it, then there is no need to trouble; (i.e. an indication that the birth canal has constricted due to heat and it's safe to proceed without further intervention)
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	but it is fitting to apply things moist and greasy; (i.e. to use soothing and lubricating agents to help ease the delivery process)
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the ointments are applied, and those in sharpness softening and moistening. (i.e. to use a type of soothing ointment or salve to help ease any discomfort or pain)
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the baby is on its side, and you can put it equal, then anoint with what we have said for the living child; (i.e. to use a soothing ointment or salve on the baby's body, just as one would for a newborn)
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if you have no power (i.e. strength or ability), then pull it out by pieces, and leave nothing of the second ligature; (i.e. to carefully remove the baby's body in sections, making sure not to leave any part behind)
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then apply the ointment that we have said on the hot swellings that come to the womb; (i.e. to use a soothing ointment or salve to help ease any discomfort or pain in the birth canal)
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding comes from the afterbirth, then apply it with restraining water, and other remedies; (i.e. to use a type of antiseptic or soothing agent to help control any bleeding that may occur during or after delivery)
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then she covered one other on top of that one, and rejected the death of the others; (i.e. the woman's uterus contained two fetuses, but only one was stillborn, while the other fetus was viable)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came out some swellings in the mouth, and swelled so much that it opened up, and began to rot; (i.e. the stillborn fetus was surrounded by a foul-smelling, decomposing tissue)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound; (i.e. despite my best efforts, I was unable to properly sew up or close the incision site)
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong ointment of attraction, and came out a bone, and after some days, another one; (i.e. the decomposing tissue and bones were slowly being released from the woman's body)
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because in that belly there is no bone; (i.e. despite my initial assumption that the swelling contained bones, it turned out to be a type of soft tissue or membrane)
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child. (i.e. I mistakenly believed that the hard, calcified material was the remains of a stillborn fetus)
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I closed the wound, and pulled out more bones, until the woman was in better condition; (i.e. I continued to carefully remove the decomposing tissue and bone fragments from the woman's body, helping her to recover)
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman was cured for a long time like that, and remained ever so slightly pale. (i.e. despite some lingering effects from her ordeal, the woman made a full recovery)
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I do not remember this chapter was finished until because of what, when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to help it; (i.e. a commentary on the importance of seeking guidance and expertise when faced with unusual or unexpected situations)
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the womb to its place. (i.e. a conclusion to the text, indicating that the discussion about childbirth and the uterus is now complete)
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, to which we owe the books; and to two turnings at two hands of the two links. (i.e. a reference to the physical characteristics or design of some tool or instrument used in bookmaking)
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns are more subtle than the restrictor, and are made of ebony or boxwood; (i.e. a description of some fine detail about the instrument, emphasizing its precision and craftsmanship)
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the handle is one palm and a half in width, and the margin of the trees (i.e. the frame or border) is one foot, and of long one palm and a half; (i.e. a description of the dimensions and proportions of some part of the instrument, likely referring to its overall size and shape)
