et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two links are two joinings of this same handle, which fasten in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; (i.e. a description of some additional feature or mechanism that attaches to the instrument's handle)
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joinings are tied in the mouth of the womb so that it opens when one turns the two horns. (i.e. a description of how the instrument's mechanism is connected to the womb, and how it operates)
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with its similarity more subtle and lighter, is made of wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pincers; (i.e. a description of another type of instrument or tool that has a similar design to pincers)
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has at two hands two joinings, just as you see, one palm long, and two fists wide; (i.e. a description of the instrument's size and shape)
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the womb with all the instrument, it makes the woman sit on one bed, legs stretched and thighs apart; (i.e. a description of how the instrument is used in conjunction with the woman's body, emphasizing her position and posture)
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then tie the two joinings together in the womb, and hold the handle of the instrument underneath her hips. (i.e. a description of how to use the instrument in conjunction with the woman's body, emphasizing its placement and positioning)
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with all the instrument, just as you have done with pincers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the womb, until the midwife makes what she wants. (i.e. a description of how to use the instrument in conjunction with the woman's body, emphasizing its effectiveness and the desired outcome)
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all perfected, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the midwives have prepared them, then the work is done more quickly, and higher in value to men for their quantity. (i.e. a conclusion that emphasizes the importance and value of these instruments in the practice of midwifery)
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	And do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for its necessity is not excusable. (i.e. a reminder to always be prepared and equipped with the necessary tools and instruments in order to properly perform one's duties)
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, it is fitting that you order the patient to hold her breath and then have her strain with condiments, and tie her hands at the mouth and navel. (i.e. a description of how to help manage the situation when there are complications during childbirth)
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she comes out easily, well done. (i.e. an expression of satisfaction or approval that the delivery has gone smoothly and without major issues)
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	And if not, take a pot and make a hole or cover it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, sarsaparilla, and centaury. (i.e. a description of how to use medicinal herbs to try and help facilitate delivery)
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or placed in hot water over the fire; then put one end of the bundle or hole of the pot and the other end into the mouth of the womb. (i.e. a description of how to use the herbal remedies in conjunction with the instrument to try and facilitate delivery)
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it burn until the vapors come out into the womb; then have her strain, as we have said. (i.e. a description of how to use the herbal remedies in combination with heat and steam to try and facilitate delivery)
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the afterbirth comes out quickly. (i.e. an expression of success or completion, indicating that the delivery has gone smoothly)
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, command the midwife to moisten her right hand with sesame oil or with mullein seed, and then put it into the womb. (i.e. a description of how to use another type of herbal remedy, mullein seed, in an attempt to facilitate delivery)
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and asks for the afterbirth; and when she has found it, then takes it and stretches it out little by little straightly, so that the womb does not tear during the extraction. (i.e. a description of how to carefully remove the afterbirth from the woman's body)
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it is fitting to move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull it out; if it comes out and separates itself. (i.e. a description of how to gently manipulate the afterbirth in order to remove it from the woman's body)
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is very constricted, we have said the treatment of straining and fumigating herbs. (i.e. a reference back to previous instructions on how to use herbal remedies and heat to try and facilitate delivery)
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not helped by all that we have said, then be cautious that you do not cause further harm. (i.e. a warning to the midwife to exercise caution and avoid causing further complications)
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is fitting that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie to the navel of the woman, then apply ointment of tetrafarmacium. (i.e. a description of how to apply a specific type of herbal ointment to help manage the situation)
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if it will make her pass and come out, but nevertheless, when she pushes and the bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient. (i.e. a warning that even if the delivery is ultimately successful, there may still be unpleasant consequences for the woman)
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is thus fitting to make fumigations that are suitable for this: no one of the ancients has tried fumigation with lettuce and dried figs. (i.e. a reference to an ancient medical practice or remedy, using fumigation as a means of treating the woman)
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at the retention of flowers and afterbirth is thus: (i.e. a description of how to use an instrument or tool to create a type of vapor or fume that can be used in conjunction with herbal remedies)
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is shaped like a bundle of twigs, and one places the delicate end in the natural orifice, and the wide hands over the fire. (i.e. a description of how to prepare and use the instrument for fumigation)
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the coals, and burn it until it is consumed, and then start another one. (i.e. a description of how to repeat the process of fumigation in order to continue treating the woman)
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (i.e. a term used to describe a medical procedure or treatment, likely referring to piercing or incising the perineal area)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born without having the fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped with a small sponge: (i.e. a description of a situation where the perineal area is not pierced during childbirth, but instead remains intact)
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is fitting for the midwife to pierce that sponge with her fist at its end, and not pierce the fundament with a sharp spatula, and guard the ligament so that it does not touch. (i.e. a description of how the midwife should carefully pierce the sponge or perineal area during childbirth)
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on linen moistened in wine and oil, then apply the treatment with ointment until it is healed. (i.e. a description of how to care for the perineal area after childbirth)
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put or make a hole with a piece of linen, and let the hands remain for days, and be removed when the child wants to go to the chambers (i.e. the perineal area may need further treatment and care after childbirth)
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or swelling, it is fitting to cover that sudden stoppage: if it is cured, as we have said of the piece of linen. (i.e. a description of how to care for and treat any unexpected complications or obstructions that may arise during childbirth)
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament (i.e. a medical condition where an abnormal connection or passageway forms between the skin and the rectum, causing leakage or discharge)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from underneath the fundament are nodulated (i.e. have a lump or swelling), and grow larger than those that come from above the fundament, or in the space between the two parts. (i.e. a description of the characteristics and differences between different types of fistulas)
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if you have a fistula or more, and when that nodulated one is old, it works (i.e. produces symptoms), and brings about a moistened white or subtle pus; (i.e. a description of the type of discharge or fluid associated with an old, nodulated fistula)
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are closed; and are known by this that there is or is not emission or windiness when the patient makes an emission, and by chance a worm comes out. (i.e. a description of how to diagnose and confirm the presence of a fistula)
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if you have fistulas that perforate just to the bladder, and just to half of the penis, and reach just to the junction of the navel and just to the knee. (i.e. a description of the extent or severity of the fistula)
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows if the fistula is closed at the fundament and not closed. (i.e. a way to determine whether a fistula has healed or remains open)
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you press your index finger or foundation, and press a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twistiness, then I press a thin tent or eyelash of horsehair into it until you feel the tent or hair at your fingertip;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is no perforation or excretion nor windiness nor boil, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it doesn't puncture; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has pierced just up to the bladder or just up to the urethra channel, then it lets out urine and cannot be healed with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has pierced just up to the crotch jointure, then the tent comes out just at the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twistiness and the inflammation of pain around it, then it is that it will go to bowel, and it doesn't help with medicine or healing by anointing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these pierced fistulas there is no strong cure other than surgery, and the vanity of foolish people who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are not pierced and are not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the sick person lies between your hands on their back; and they lift up their legs until above their crotch, and have their crotch inclined towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a sheet of iron or a thin tent if there is twistiness, as much as you know that the tent reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the sick person feels it around the fundament, then it's fitting that you insert your index fingers there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if then it feels that the tent has pierced; and you discover something between your finger and the scrotum or the skin, then know that it is pierced.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if there is no swelling, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is always said that some can be well cured, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help we do is that we heat up a small cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and insert it all hot into the fistula, as far as it will reach near the fundament; and do this two or three times, as much as you know that the charred parts are burnt, which are similar to a bird's quill.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moistened tents in grease, as long as the charred parts show through; and then cure it with anointing oil that heals and seals the wounds.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus cleansed, it is well. Otherwise, it cannot be cleansed otherwise.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the stone pierces, but does not go through to the bottom which is the fundament, and between your navel and the stone there is a covering thick with fat or flesh, and you see the fistula at that place who ends the covering from the inside;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you sew it up at the beginning of the fistula, and plug it right away before the stone, and cauterize afterwards, as long as it reaches to the head of the stone;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the stone will come out and fall away; then remove those cut-off pieces of flesh that resemble a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain comes back to you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or a hot medicament.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cauter of fire does two things: to wit, it dries up those cut-off pieces of flesh that are stuck together, and it dries out blood and moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of moistened tents in butter or cheese broth, as long as the sore emits pus, and let the burnt flesh come out through the pus.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with ointments of sudden healing in greasy flesh, and are the dry medicaments.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, then plug it with your finger or fundament, and investigate inside.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the stone and it is between two things, either the cloth or the bladder or flesh, where it is about to pierce, then there are no more ways that can be seen of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you sew it up all the way to the bottom, or if you can't, then let tents and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and don't go too far in depth, that you don't sew up the compartment that holds the fundament, and comes out through the opposite side willingly.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it is healed, or you remove that covering and clean it then since it has been sewn up next to the fundament, either by a tent or by another instrument appointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse that foul flesh in the wound as long as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to close the fistula in the part outside the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the sick person.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And at no time does the fistula according to this manner: and is when you plug the tent in the fistula, and it is on one side of the fundament next to the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a pointed needle at its head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and I put one twisted thread in two, and plug the needle into all the thread in the fistula as far as its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the edge of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that punctured one, just as you would plug your finger or fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull out the head of the thread, and join together the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and let it stay like that for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and bind it at no time, until the thread copes those flesh parts that are between them, and close together.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound as long as it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to pierce the binding that has been sewn up too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinal needle from which one makes the fistula is very acute on both sides and pointed.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not so much, for this reason one does not pierce what one should not pierce, as you see here:
des emorroydes	nerves.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Nerves are in two ways: either they are inside the fundament, just like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in their cortex, they have been cut.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have less moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and in their cortex, they have a little bit of clear water or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the care for those that are inside the fundament, is that you command the sick person to strain so they can relieve themselves into a chamber pot, until the fundament comes out and the thread becomes apparent.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it with tweezers or at your fingernail, then cut it in its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the thread cannot be held by itself because of its moisture, then take it on a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder over warm powders that serve as cauterization.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them just like it is said in the book of cauterization, then cure them with other remedies until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot come out, then purge the sick person with a purgative potion that is bitter and sharp to wash away what is in the fundament, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the sick person feels relieved and the thread is free from the fundament, then the remedy is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it's that you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that the sick person will no longer fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you stitch the wound in this manner: take a twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then pull out the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two heads of the thread under the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is wide; and bind the thread tightly, then knot the thread, pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for correcting the excess of blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the fundament a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the fundament, and command the sick person to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him be until he is quiet, and when they are calm, then treat them with ointment and other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the healing of the anus or fundament.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often times there is a healing of the anus in the intestines, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you scratch at the tip of a splinter or with your fingernail the scab on top, which prevents it from becoming wet.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is sound, as necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it is sound and scabbed over.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of hemorrhoids.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A furuncle is a small, false appearance around the body, and it goes quite deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and at times the boil bursts, and the pain is just like that of a furuncle, and comes to the entire body, and is more severe than in other places.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a piece of candle from a goose quill or a strong feather, and put that wick on the furuncle, until the heat makes the furuncle turn red all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then twist your hand around the entire candle until you cut all around the furuncle, and put it deep, and extract the furuncle from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see [fit], then make it with a wire of iron or steel in this shape, and be thin under and twisted above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and squeeze it And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is written in the book of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the cathartic.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times one makes a cathartic of silver or lead, or melted tin or alloyed metal; and at times one makes these instruments small and large, according to the shape in which they are made.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, the ones that are made for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the cathartic, big or small, is above wide, or the belly is joined in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening or the belly is joined, as you see, and the pipe is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it is the belly where the medicine is put from a bladder of animal or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has between each hole a thread of twine, then put into the holes one strong thread of twisted cord in ten or eleven turns, and tie up the belly as a she-goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then bind it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, and catharticize; and this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the top of the cathartic with oil or egg yolk, or a similar thing, then put it in lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the servants should press the cathartic with both hands together until it is completely full, then pull out the cathartic, and raise the sick person's legs to the bed.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then pull on it as long as it can; and if he sleeps all night completely, then it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catharticize him in the sickness of intestinal obstruction, and the medicine comes out quickly, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or swelling, then the cathartic should be just as fine as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the fine cathartic on which the skin should be stretched.
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatments of hands and of medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things from which wounds are made are by being struck with a stone, and cut with a sword or knife, or with a lance or club or spear, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or the wounds are made in various parts of the body, such as a wound that cuts on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will start with the simple head wounds, because the memory will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from being struck with a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you slightly doubt an abscess from heat: if it makes the wound heal quickly with a poultice made of its own head, and there is pus coming out from the wound, and it heals in the opposite part of the damaged area.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and give the sick person a diet of wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it doesn't want to heal, then decrease the amount of meat and don't let him drink wine or eat roasted meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound a compress of damp cotton soaked in rose oil or wine spirits, if an abscess comes.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess from heat, then put on the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood and not touched by air or dust, a powder that I will say about later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has spoiled it, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword or similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then stitch them together with sutures, just as I will say about belly wounds, in the chapter of suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered of bone and bleeds profusely and can only be held together with a piece of cloth, then cut it away. Then treat the wound with medicine and replace hard skin in place of soft skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the sick person to eat thick meats, such as roasted chestnuts and wheat, also chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a gangrene on the skin that has not reached the bone, then cut out all of it and throw away the pus, and then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it, loosen it, and tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: you put on this powder which heals even when the air has spoiled it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making the powder is this: take equal parts of frankincense and dragon's blood, three parts of red calamine, and powder it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it is completely healed and the skin joins together with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then tie it well, and let it be until it comes off by itself, without being untied, because the medicine is not removed as long as the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times we make this with calamine alone, when we do not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but only when the air has spoiled the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the air has completely spoiled the wound, even in its depth, then put on this powder nowhere.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments or poultices made of wheat flour, water and honey, until it purges.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments as long as it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put any thing restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the wound be moist with medicine such as calamine dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and tie with bandages, and treat it as long as it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have a lot of pus, then drain them or lower them to a point below.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then tie it off, bind it tight, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut or the gullet, and the duct that conducts food, is guarded, by which the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so sew up the gullet on the cord of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it tightly and leave it for some days, then treat it with digestive ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cauterize it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then extract them all as soon as possible, and leave the wound alone until it becomes gangrenous.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and make a cut and tie off the discharge.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have said about earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then look to see if the patient feels windiness coming up: know at once that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then don't put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that doesn't clot in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and returns to the heart and kills the sick person.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out all the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the sick person sleep on the wound for three days, or four days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if it doesn't come to him as a spasm, or evil trembling of the heart, or distress of vomiting.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with stitches and other treatments as long as it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it can't heal and there's a bad smell, then know that there's a fistula; treat it as you should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or dagger, and it's simple, or worse, or on the back, so that the treatment is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it's large, sew it up; and if it's small, dust powder on it, and if it's embedded in the bone and has splintered pieces, clean the wound and sew up the lacerations.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not torn, leave the wound to suppurate, as it will bring faster relief.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs let the judgement be as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from dislocation of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The dislocations of the belly are great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound the intestines often burst out or the membranes of the intestines, through which their introduction.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the sewing up is more difficult, and sometimes it's worse than the small wound that the large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason one puts back the intestines with pins only if they are not put back hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they don't go back in with pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore the middle-sized wound is better, because one sews up the intestine to its place more quickly than with the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common sutures happen in the sewing up of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and anyway they are more proper with the suturing of the belly, and I will say each one and declare them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I will translate the text line-by-line without any additional comments.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and there is another thing to do, which is by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm him in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one soft cloth in hot water, only.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil in hot water of squinancy and cypress and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and warm the intestines as long as the swelling is gone.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and when you have done this wine, it restrains and is used only to unswell.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestines with hot water or ale and let them be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by that is loosened the entrée to take little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small hole in the wound with the instrument of which we cut off hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is used only for cutting.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without great necessity, since there is no need.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument for cutting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	cut inside in the curvature and then outwards, and you will see its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines have burst forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its natural place according to its proper shape.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you cannot do this, for it is worth nothing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part under the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so that you cause the sick person to lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part under the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and chest higher than the parts under;
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then put your understanding into that which the hurt part be higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to apply what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Apply a salve to small wounds as you are accustomed.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then take it in your hands, i.e., the ministrer poultice that clings to the whole form of the arm.
et assemble les levres;	and close the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is a common way of bandaging.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound's breadth.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at once from the head of the wound, that is to say two fingers' breadth, and insert one needle where there will be good strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two cheeks of the leather with the two eyes of the needle.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that side.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and tie together the two eyes of the needle and the four ends.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then wind a doubled thread around the needle from both sides.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then tie together the two ends of the wound together.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave two fingers' breadth, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread so as you have tied the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you need more needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is encircled.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and that the needles be worn out, fine and coarse.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well get in:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is convenient that they be worn out.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not suit to push the needles too far into the flesh and the leather.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they will pierce and gape the wound in front of the scar.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put thread or cloth on the ends of the needles to keep them from falling out.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is closed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it suffices to have one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you tie together the two cheeks of the leather and the two eyes of the thread together with one needle or where there is one strong doubled thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced those cheeks altogether, four ends.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then tie the needle to the part where you began, in the manner of sewing clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch, the thickness of two little fingers.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is known as the "homme" or "man's stitch",
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that had been made on the belly of a man,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's breadth in size.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it went so deep that the intestines were exposed, two palms' breadth.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I pulled the intestines back into place, and he had been without them for 24 hours by now.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was closed in exactly 15 days, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in one place where there was none to be found, nor any other medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put clean cotton on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and push it from the outer part to the inner part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the leather straight through, then take the end of the thread or cord where you put in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inner part to the outer part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew as the tailor does with furs.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you leave the thread once on one side and take it back up again from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of sewing, which the Galicians call properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to sew them together naturally, just like those who assemble two parts together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they apply one end of the thread to the other end, in that manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	stick a needle or the end of the thread close by, and make it pierce just that spot.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and grab both ends of the thread again.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce from one end to the other through both ends of the thread, in two other holes that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Galicians say these words, and many testify to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the stomach with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and you must put one needle from this side and the other from that side, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the stomach,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitch more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as if fire had changed it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the skin, and then place on top the powder of white charcoal.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if fire has changed it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut off the thread, and sew up the cord, and the needle.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on old cotton cloth, as soon as she starts to heal slowly.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in most cases, since the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not become a community of members primarily,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is advisable to mix linen light oil with temperate hot oil or with rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the armpits and under the shoulders.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or foulness in the bowels, and many times has happened,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse him with wine made from black grapes, and also if the foulness comes as far as the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and perforate it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easy to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestines called "jun" cannot be healed if they are injured.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the looseness and softness of their veins, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to that of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the spleen bursts from the wound, put it back in place as well as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned green or black, then it is advisable that you tie the place which is black, so that no bleeding comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the tie,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put both ends of the thread on either side of the wound from bottom to top so that it eases the bleeding when the spleen bursts and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are twisted, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly with a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into an ulcer, and there was discharge and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not stop purifying until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it close up, I doubted that the illness would return in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no more harm, but he stayed in better condition, eating and drinking well.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and expert physicians said that when someone has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh gauze from great fennel plants, then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the gauze has opened up the mouth, put it on top of both lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it tightens its mouth shut again.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then tie the top of it, and so it stays like that, so that he cannot untie it.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another gauze on top in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That head will stay in the intestine and cause no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is attached to the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread which is somewhat separated from the animal's intestine,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie it to the end of that fine linen thread that has been twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread into a needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie it in the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with gauze is nothing but according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is big and wide, even when it is in one of the gallbladder intestines, there is no remedy nor healing, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an ulcer or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is grown and has begun to heal.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true hard and white nodule formation where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also grown as the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts out clear and open, and other times it becomes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and other times large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but due to one of the eight reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh.
ou por sa malice;	or because it is malignant.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard skin inside and on the edges of the wound that does not allow new skin to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much discharge.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is foul and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in that region, the digestion is slow, and health takes time to heal, and is naturally inclined towards corruption.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by hand's work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come to the main veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder, or to any of the intestines, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is such that it comes to the proper place of the principal limb, and to its apparent location.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas which are in this manner are of great danger, and there is no other treatment except surgery, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you are confident of its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it clearly, if you take a tent made of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, sew it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, search for a subtle patch of leather,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the leather will bend more easily around its winding.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot cover it well with patches,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	use a catheter through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture runs from one hole to another and cleans it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then sew it up with your skill, as you know whether there are bones or nerves, and cut deep enough.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you know the true location of the pain, and whether it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you, if so, cut according to what I have said.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the dead tissue and corrupted flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then heal it until it is sound.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well located in a straight place, sew in deep, as long as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist patches on medicated linen and soak them up to the top of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess tissue that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put ointments of fresh and clean fat until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then scald it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves are in your way or main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, wash it thoroughly until all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then dress it with fresh fat as long as it takes to heal.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, then return to the previous method as we said before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	be aware that you have not gone far enough:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	expose and cut until you reach the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, be aware that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot proceed further;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy than to let it heal by its own nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	extract it with an instrument suitable for this.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, put on the wound something that will spoil and rot.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the place around the bones is rotten.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be more easily removable.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	wash thoroughly only the corruption until all the blackness is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there's a large part of the corrupted tissue and it reaches almost to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is advisable to scrape out and cut all the way up to the corruption, and then dress it until it heals.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in one man's leg;
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you can take it as an example and guide in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body;
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the materials came to the leg and he was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no apparent cause from outside to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physicians by their folly opened it so high that the abscess burst open.
