et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in consequence there came out a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there were many pus-filled tunnels that all went down to the body's moisture.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians put medicine around it for two years, and there was no skill in their handwork.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what came out through the tunnels in large quantities;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became reddish and had a yellowish-citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I sewed up one of these tunnels with a stitch, and then I searched all the other tunnels;
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some came together with others from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So then I hurried and cut into one of the tunnels until I uncovered a part of the bone;
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption was coming up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for the one that I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and then I began to repair the wound with soothing medicines over a long period of time, and it did not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and exposed the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I extracted it, and I thought to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and then I extracted it all the way to its marrow.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I repaired it with medicine, and it was healed and sound very quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the sick person, who could not bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the evacuation it would often bleed profusely, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone there was formed a hard skin, and he had good health and suffered no harm or evil at all, neither when healing nor when recovering.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be scraped out in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and stretch it to the head of the bone which is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another linen cloth, which is thicker than the first one, and tie it above the skin that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you can draw out the corrupted skin below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin above the place where you see it being scraped, so that the scraping does not damage the skin.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot ember or a heated spatula below the bone to melt and cover the corrupted skin;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and scrape away until you can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it;
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the skin, then put a hot ember under it;
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one part to the other until you reach the length of the corruption, just as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and scrape away the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the joining of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut them off.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, then it is very strong and difficult.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you must investigate that decay, how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but beware of the vein or nerve that may cause you harm.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the saw and the scrapers for cutting these bones are many, according to the size of the bone and its appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work in appearance;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work itself will show you the instrument that you need, according to your knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument that you need, according to what it is necessary.
dou feu	from fire;
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can decay or deteriorate due to a cause from within, or due to an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried the medicine on that corruption and it does not bring relief,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member all the way up to where the decay comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the sick person may escape through death or through healing, which is greater, from the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the members become black, as if they were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then it turns a pale color after becoming black, and the decay of the member spreads to other members.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of everything in the body; so hasten to cut out.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to a sting from some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	so cut out the decay in the head of the vein, and do not give it any space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, cut it out at the wrist, so that the decay does not come into the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy or cure except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and similarly do this when the decay comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it out after the second joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises into the leg, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die from death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or scraping the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and have two attendants stretch one end of the string downwards and another attendant hold the other end upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the skin that is between the two strings with a wide spatula until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut it out or scrape it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the scraping does not touch the healthy area.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another inflammation and boil will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs during the operation, then cauterize the place quickly;
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put some constricting powders on it, and then come back to your medication until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bandage the injured member with a convenient strip of cloth, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in my town:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a blackness that seemed like burn scars from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the decay came first to his vein of the foot, spreading all the way through it;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the decay, he hastened to cut off the foot and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the decay returned to his vein of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him remedies after purifying his body, but the corruption did not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of recovering the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's vitality was weak; and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told you this story only because of the things that one does in extremity, when they are necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At times a boil forms on a fleshy area and stays for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and bursts open, and the pus jumps out, and the area is left clean, just like a vessel that has been rinsed.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that remains above is just as delicate as a finely woven silk cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not spread to the bone or nerve, and diseases like this are called "healthy". (Note: This seems to be a play on words, as "sain" is Old French for "sound" or "healthy", but it's likely being used here in a more ironic sense, implying that this type of disease is not actually healthy at all.)
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula". (A fistula is an abnormal connection or passage between two body parts, often resulting from disease or injury.)
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches to the bone deep inside, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must cut off all around it, and just as much when it becomes delicate, like a silk cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have confidence that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in the deepest part,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a poultice like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine if the swelling is large and the pus that comes out has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then apply an Egyptian remedy made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloe, oil, and litarium (litargirium), equally, and put the mixture in a vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take what you need from it and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and apply the poultice to the swelling, and tie up the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for two hours, then take it out by squeezing it gently.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the swelling is reduced and the pus is completely drained out.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is fomented with ashes' water.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not available, and you take ash from grapevine wood, and pour water on it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it cool down, and use it as a poultice, until you know that the swelling is well reduced.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, then neither the Egyptian remedy nor water of ashes can be used.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then apply a poultice made with water and honey, or mix in a little bit of ground litargirium.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or make the poultice with honey and sweet wine, so that the honey's property of purifying and cleansing can be used.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound heal quickly.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and have confidence that the swelling is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then apply a poultice with what makes new flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take defrutum and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or apply a poultice made of some medicines and ointments, whose properties or uses I have mentioned in the treatment of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the swelling is small and the poultice cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it a little with an iron point, and put in a tent made of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, as long as it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only a small area or opening where the poultice can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that discharges pus is on top, then cut it off or lower the area so that it is not.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	because when the pus is deep inside, it does not allow flesh to grow back.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the swelling from below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare it in such a way that the pus drains to the lowest point of the wound.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep inside, it does not allow flesh to grow back.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut out the swelling from below as you see fit,

pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound.

car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the health is approaching. For there are men whose wounds in their flesh take too long to heal, and those who do the opposite;

puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and this same thing makes better cooked honey thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphinite ointment is not present,

et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then apply it, that is to say, a dressing, and extend it over the breast, and do not administer it again for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and the roots of lily which are also like flour of dates and centaury;

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of this disease is like the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the aposteme of an ulcer.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pus is a suppurating lesion that forms under the skin of the palm of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, or perhaps it arises in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes old and one does not take care of it, if it comes to a foul suppurating ulcer.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and flow freely as long as the root of the ulcer is still present, and perhaps they will continue to do so until it is all gone.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion just up to the bone, as long as there is a foul-smelling pain, and the hole of the fistula is wide and has a greenish-yellow color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not bring any benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut out entirely all the remaining superfluity of the ulcer,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the ulcer is clean.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the ulcer has eaten into the flesh, and begun to suppurate, and form an abscess,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a lint or cloth under the ulcer that has formed a sore.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tightly, and carefully cut out the thin and delicate flesh underneath.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh some medicinal ointments that are burning and corrosive to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has gone into the bone, then cut out that part, and treat the area with a poultice, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see that the bone is corrupting, then cut out a piece of flesh from above as it was said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering and inflamed, and causes great pain, then it is necessary that you treat the ulcer first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut out the ulcer of the suppurating abscess diagonally from above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not come too close to the flesh under the ulcer, for the sick person would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on it that will soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the earache of the hand ( possibly a reference to a specific medical condition).
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fistula that arises in some people's hands, perhaps due to their being excessively fatty.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and it may happen that there is a small boil or an ulcer on it, and sometimes even a fistula.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them arise at the root of the joint, or in some of the bones of the hands.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that arise in any part of the hand do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that arise at the joint of the hand, perhaps it does move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is fatty is light and easy, in a similar way,
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it out from its root with a wide abscess.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who arises at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, so you should take care not to cut into it too deeply.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In him who arises in or at the last part of the hand, it is necessary that you cut out the surrounding flesh all the way to the bone first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut out the bone with a suitable thread for that, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes on the hand together with others comes from birth, or from a blow, or from being burned by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out the swelling, and then repair the finger so that it heals according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two cloths or moistened napkins in rose oil, so that they do not become swollen again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin linen cloths, until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that swelling in the manner that is necessary.
Des vils	It seems like you're switching to a new topic. "Vil" can be translated to "villain" or "wretch", so it's likely that the text will describe some kind of medical condition affecting the skin, perhaps acne or similar issues associated with poor hygiene or other negative factors.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The boils are foul-smelling, large and inflamed, filled with melancholy suppurations, that come on various members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they are more prone to occur in the legs of those who walk and work and bear weight, than on others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer them sometimes a purging of gall, and then cleanse them with the lily of the valley (a plant-based remedy).
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment by fire is according to two manners: one is when they are cut out and then treated with a poultice the black ichor.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you lance the boil and let it run its course until it is fully drained.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: first, arise the leg with a hot iron very strongly, until the thick skin is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then take away the leg of the sick person from above the knee down to the part under the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut out the boil in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a wide cut.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift up and let drain the black ichor to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the sick person can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it up, and command him to eat savory meat with black gall to make a dark complexion.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and the cleansing when the boils are full and painful to the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment of the swelling is in this manner: take away the leg of the sick person if there is too much hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water as high as it can be carried, so that the swelling increases.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it up over the fire, and then cut into the boil in a long incision from the top of the knee or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with the hot iron, and flay the boil from each side, until it is apparent when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it will be red and black, and when it enters the skin it will seem like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then bind it tight underneath, until it is raised out of the skin, and then let it dry with the light iron.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place above three fingers, then flay the skin over the boil until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up to the iron, just like you did before, and let it dry with another hot iron, just like you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if necessary, then lift it up and cut it at the bone of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then let it drain and lift up as far as the second incision, then pull it out of incision to incision, until all the ichor comes out, and then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot drain it and lift it up, then insert an awl into each thread tightly doubled.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and let drain it, and insert underneath one end of the thread, and turn your hand from side to side until all comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then it cannot be drained or lifted, and it will cause harm to the sick person.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drained it all, then put a wet wool cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the boil is contracted and twisted and inflamed together, and it is not straight, as we have said... si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you split it unevenly, but do not cut it off; and drain it just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the boil is curved, and does not cut straight, so that it may cut into the boil.

De la voinne civile	It seems that the text is switching to a new topic. "La Voinne Civile" can be translated to "The Civil Boil", which suggests that the following text will describe a boil or an abscess of a specific type, possibly one that occurs in people who are not sick or unhealthy.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This boil is generated in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it may also arise in other parts than the legs, and this happens from filth that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	such as it arises inside the body of serpents and worms, generated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this boil are that it comes in the leg as a great inflammation.
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the boil begins to come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the boil opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a cloth of linen from one and a half to two and a half feet, and then tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth hang at the leg, and every time it becomes wet, wrap it around the cloth and tie it again.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part around it, and do not cut it in its root until it has come out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and filth or boil in that place, and a great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	in order to avoid this evil thing it is necessary that it be treated gradually and little by little up to the end, and nothing of it remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and at times this boil, when treated, is as long as five palms or ten.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once upon a time a man came to me, from whom it came out ten palms long, and when you cut it, a vein or artery bursts, and it bleeds until the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the matter inside is emptied, and medicine to prevent filth is administered to the place every day, then it is treated just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at times this boil comes in multiples, and especially when it breaks out in the joint of the foot, or on the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it bursts into many veins, and from which there come forth many abscesses; then treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	It seems like the text is switching to a new topic. "Vers" can be translated to "worms", so this section will likely describe a medical condition related to worms or parasites that live between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it has afflicted many times with oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that lives between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body, going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it causes great pain to anyone who feels its movement from member to member, until it bursts through the skin where it is going and comes out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it generates filth from various humors, just like worms and serpents and lice and ascarides that live in the intestines.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and we doubt its wickedness, because when it travels through the body and goes up to the head and comes into the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only be sure that it is cured when it comes out:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong thread, tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and let drain, and if the worm is deeply in the flesh and you don't find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize with fire on top, until it chars.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it causes is that it goes into the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near to the eye, then take hold of it with a pair of tweezers and cut on top and let drain.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary for the sick person to use cleansing remedies for the body, dissolving bad humors that cause the disease.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of savory meats that cause filth.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	It seems like the text is switching to a new topic. "Dolor" can be translated to "pain", and "ventositie" means "windiness". This section will likely describe a medical condition related to pain caused by wind or gas in the body.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into certain members, probably referring to the abdominal region.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then spreads from member to member; and I have seen this myself, which I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the boil of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and a little while later, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	almost immediately, as quickly as live silver when it melts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and a little while later it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she was twisting around her body, as I had seen myself.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how she moved from member to member, as I had never seen this disease in that manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had heard that many people well knew the pain to move from one place to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it myself, as I did in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the woman's body was dry and her boils were open,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore the windiness of the body is revealed.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in this way to those who are healthy, and have moist bodies and closed boils.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the disease being treated, and the sick person feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then... (it seems like the text is interrupted)
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if you bind it above and below quickly, and then cut on top until that windiness of the body comes out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you don't see it at your own hands.
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with those things that purge the windiness, such as foul-smelling pills and serpent's pill and similar ones.
Des saiettes	It seems like the text is switching to a new topic. "Saiettes" can be translated to "splinters", so this section will likely describe a medical condition related to splinters or foreign objects that have entered the body.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their shapes and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and thorny, and splintered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two corners, and those with tongues, and those with fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that one which falls in some member falls either directly into the principal part, or it splits off into two parts.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any of these parts, and the sign of death that I will tell you later becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must beware of extracting this splinter, because death comes afterwards in several ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if you don't see this bad sign and the splinter is not deeply in, then drain it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the splinter falls into it and pierces the bone, and makes a hole above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when you see spots and a swollen face and an inverted face color, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and it may also cause excessive bleeding from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps impair speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and it causes an oozing white discharge from the wound, similar to pus, and also like blood from the flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then beware of the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrowhead when it falls or is bent are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrowhead moves as well as the pulse, and in black blood, and comes with cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowhead which does not penetrate the body is that without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead falls in the covering of the stomach, it is near the small ribs; and makes great anguish and great pain and gasps; and moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls on the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls in the belly, and nothing comes out through the intestines first, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead falls in the bladder, and the urine comes out and goes away, and the patient feels very painful, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and forearm and calf and knee and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you it happened to me, for that reason do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to me, that is to say, in my home with an arrow that fell or slipped into the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without any sense.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye under the eyelid.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was set back, and I could not draw out anything but the tip towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, to all the light iron without ears; the wound was healed, and no bad accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled on the barbs, and sharpened it so much that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew out an arrow from a man, who had fallen onto his belly, and thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after passing 30 days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrowhead and sharpened it, and drew it out cleanly, and he did not have any bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man to whom an arrow had fallen onto the back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural condition did not change.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man to whom an arrow had fallen into his face, and the wound was sewn up on his cheek;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I drew out an arrow from one of the king's nobles, who had fallen into his navel;
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and he was somewhat declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely set back
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to the care after it had fallen three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I touched it with a very fine needle and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on him a poultice both attracting and digestive, so that the place would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the point of the arrow appeared;
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on it the poultice for a full nine days, and the wound was healed again, and the patient remained in that state for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so much so that he felt the arrow one day inside his navel; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine of strong corrosive acid for nine days, until it was completely open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I touched it and felt the head of the arrow which was corroding at the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed well through the ends in about four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then it healed so that I could put tongs on both sides of the wound and not let it come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to try and sharpen in various ways with instruments, until I finally got it one day with tongs well made.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	in accordance with what its form will come to the end of this chapter, until I drew it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot convey everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters learn much from little things and what is currently present and deficient.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	found nine works and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit from limbs where they are lodged except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the point where they entered, or from another direction;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes out on the opposite side of where it enters is an arrow entering into fleshy places and going out again immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out now, then leave it so that the flesh around it becomes rotten and the exit is revealed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and similarly if it is lodged in a bone and cannot exit, then leave it so for some days and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if not, then pierce around with a very fine needle, so that the area around it is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes right up to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and if some of the accidents that I mentioned occur to the patient: then do not draw it out, but leave it so until it is equalized after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes right up to the brain's ventricles, that's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not come right up to the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out, then administer theriacs around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead has sunk into the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then search for it thoroughly in the wound.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you can feel it, then draw it out with any convenient instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then cut through until the wound is large enough.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow that hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut off the flesh that is lodged to both sides until you can grasp it with your hands.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow itself, but rather to draw it out more smoothly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot draw it out at once, then leave it so that the flesh around it becomes rotten, and then draw it out, because the extraction will be revealed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting into the nerve and the vein, and use your ingenuity to find a way to draw out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient in the form that he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is the greatest aid if he can be so, and if you cannot, then put him in the position that the signs show him to have been in.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes out from the opposite side, or where it has caused some appearance of damage, or if the skin is swollen in the area where it can be seen or felt apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut there on, until the tongs can take hold of it, and then draw it out: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is inside, then drive it all the way back into the shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft splinters and you need to administer gently, then use a sharp instrument to remove it slowly.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hairs of the instrument; and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is splintered, then insert the sharp instrument into the point of entry to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead is embedded, then it is advisable that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as seems best.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead has splintered or broken in the flank, belly, bladder, or intestines, and is close to an organ, and you can operate on it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting into the vein or nerve, and then draw it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to draw out arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the sharp instrument is also like a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	so that you can insert it at the tip of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs to put in and to check if there, is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common blood vessels of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one bleeds are xxxi, and in which there is a head or main branch xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say, the two pipes that are behind the ears, which are called "herbeches".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead, and the veins that are on top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two carotid arteries which are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins from which one bleeds commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is of the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the second one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the ribcage.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one from which one bleeds, which appears clearly on top of the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvatelle vein is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the left scrotum,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is the saphena that is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein called "nesse" which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient catarrh and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the bled, as I told you, is that you rinse the head of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wring out the wound or the veins with a rough cloth, then bind the patient's neck with a string.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependent places of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	question them then to your shoulder, and where you feel the pulse under your shoulder, if it is softening.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and insert it through under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the whole length of the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and take out the skin and the vein as far as the crossing of the shoulders, and let the blood come out until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then sew it up and bind it tightly, so that it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about the incision and cauterizing in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for ancient migraine.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and also, eye sickness and accustomed headache, and at the core of tears of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bled are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens their neck, until the two veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse under your shoulder, and then softens.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift up the skin over the vein upwards towards the index finger of your hand, and insert the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you did with the other two veins, and let out the blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your hand on top of the vein for an hour, then put some cotton on top.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it tightly, and let it be until it is healed; and we have already spoken of its cutting and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is worth just as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for ancient facial illnesses, and for migraine, and for roup.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient tightens their neck in twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on top of the vein, and press down with your hand or other thing, and let out as much blood as you see fit.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein tightly until it is healed, and that no bleeding occurs with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable that the bleeding be too abundant and cross over, because the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the bleeding when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the corners of the eyes helps with eye diseases, and for conjunctivitis, and for roup, and for inflammation in the eye, and for facial illnesses.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck in twisting with any string, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it bleed, and the bleeding of the trunk be about half a long finger in width, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bleeding is subtle, it may break through; then let out the blood, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding from the vein of the nose is worth for ague, and for acute fever, and for facial illnesses.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraine and roup that come to the face, and especially when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, then binds their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a fine and long thread, and insert it between the two nostrils in the space that is between the nose.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it go too deep, and let out the blood as much as you need, then bind it for a night, because it is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that's the shape of the thread:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding from the two carotid arteries helps with the constriction of the lungs, and with the beginning of consumption, and with many diseases, and with epilepsy, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and with eruptions.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck under one and the other carotid artery, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and it should be the master's hands on top of the patient's head, and the patient sees them on one side.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then let out the blood from the vein as long as is necessary, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as need be.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other part in the other vein, then release the string, and bind around the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke, and let it be until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	The bleeding from the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding from the veins above the upper lips helps with mouth ulcers, and gum decay, and cracks in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and bind their neck as I said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right side of the upper lip and the other on the left side.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by their color being black, and by the fact that around them there are small dark veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then cut one or both of them, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	The bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding from the veins under the tongue also helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and they lift their tongue, and look under it on each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So then both are healthy, and do not go too deeply, for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The common wounds from which we commonly get healthy are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by being pierced all the way through with a hot iron lance, or with a subtle olive oil as is used for incised wounds, and it is called "anequil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the wounds.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the hot iron lance is very well known, and it is long as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open wounds that are quite full of thick, visible blood, and which contain thick and murky blood;
