et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive oil lance:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle to pierce, and it is for healing fine wounds, in which there is thin yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the boil, which is one of these wounds, helps against diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is suitable for the surgeon to heal the boil, and to warn him of the artery that is under it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great deal of blood comes out, then the wound needs to be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be pierced with the hot iron lance, but rather cut like an Anasil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the boil does not open up clearly, it's necessary to drain it, and change to another [boil]
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want some discharge from it, or you heal in its place the wound in the arm: it opens up clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut it with the hot iron lance of Anasil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the boil, it's necessary then that you drain the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the wound of the hot iron lance of Anasil;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hurt the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: flee from it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out in the same way as a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your hand above for a long time, then take out your hand if the bleeding stops, which has happened many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm tightly, and leave it thus, and do not move it until the sick person is healed; and be on guard, and do not move it at all until they are sound.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it flows fast, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens up, because the head of the vessel [artery] will retract; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of fig-tree, and split it in two, and take one of the halves and bind well up to just below the other joint.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding is stopped, it's good; if not, then apply a remedy, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not greasy in many dispositions for the small wound and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the wound on the arm helps so much that it stops blood from flowing out from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be cautious so that he does not touch the nerve which is below, and if he probes too deeply and finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the wound becomes greasy, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve often opens up and in some men due to its subtlety, it's necessary that you let the wound heal with the instrument of Anasil; and flee from the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is blood between the two nerves, cut it of length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The wound on the cephalic vein helps so much that it stops bleeding from the head and also helps itself.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal with a point of hot olive oil or hot myrrh oil, because it is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerve or artery below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it's necessary to seek the lightest wound, and do nothing if we don't succeed the first time, and then try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the wounds swell in some men when we fail the first time, but they do not hurt anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the healing is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about healing is that healing is not possible without preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and in order to prevent diseases from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the healing is done in one of the three ways that are or cut through: to wit, cephalic, fistula, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must heal at the beginning of spring and after eating in autumn and winter when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must heal on the first day or the third after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for diseases has no specific hour determined, but whenever need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to heal children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying fruit than the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one heal the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And whenever someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner it may be, they should purge the intestines with a light cathartic.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much foul matter retained, so that the veins do not draw out the superfluities bearing harm to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal those who are too full of meat, nor drunk, until they are clear, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and it is worse to heal after a passionate colic, vomiting, and diarrhea of the belly, and a multiplicity of dwelling with a woman, and of traveling, watching, and working, and all that the virtue, or by thing of arm or of body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purge the humors, if the blood is gross, with meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath or a shower, if nothing else hinders, to purge the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal yourself of the venom of the belly around the third day, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be joyful and glad, and let the healer be higher than he whom one heals, and have him rub the arm two times or three.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the ligature on top gently, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot correct the blood.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub it with the hands lightly until the veins swell and feel good;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the healer with the flame of a flask of old oil, then put his fist on top of that swelling in the region where he wants to heal.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the swelling does not burst and burst into the wound.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are swellings that come out like cords when healing, and some of this kind that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts on the flame, it retreats to the flame, and cannot open the swelling, and thus are such ones.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts out in the swelling, then the wound is too tight, for this reason it behooves the healer to be wise in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts out the first time, it is good; but if not, then it begins again a little below that place or above hastily, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is inflamed and the patient fears, then let it be left for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come good abscesses; do not take a bath, then resume the healing if it pleases you.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the puncture is small or the blood runs off subtly and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then stick the very same needle into the puncture itself with the flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it works a little hastily, so that the swelling is inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the swelling inflamed, do not resume the healing, and put a little linen oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is soothing in this swollen place, like the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linen oil in every healing of veins that you heal, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this very thing is done with vinegar and egg white, when one puts it on the swelling; it purifies the blood and disperses it when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens when the wound is not properly healed at that time or when the opening of the swelling is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten and put on the swollen area a sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar for a short hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding has stopped from the swelling, and if there remains at the place for any days a blackness or greenish color, then it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see fit, apply something made from aloe or myrrh, reconstituted in wine, vinegar, or similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance have occurred in the healing of the Basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to apply anything from what we have said, for it may cut off the blood from the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the wounds according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see that it is abundant, let it continue until it subsides; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for those who are robust and strong, and need the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and have wider incisions.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and make them heal slowly and frequently, and one must heal them by cutting at an angle, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of healing is safe from the risk of bleeding and bruising the nerve, and it is worth more than the healing by length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for him whose body is overheated from the healing, it is necessary to give him a damp compress soaked in juice of green apples; if he is heated up, treat the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he has a cold complexion, mix before the healing a damp compress in sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he pants from the healing, after the flow of fresh blood, it is necessary that he inhale a broth of meat and a fragrant and subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and follow the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the swelling.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to stretch his arm and heal another time, so it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds in small amounts, little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to stretch his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another part, he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood inside the body that is already heated up, and causes fever; so it needs to be drawn out in a great quantity, and to stretch the wound as wide as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you bind all the bleeding wounds, and put your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that the clot may not come in place of a scab.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the leech is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it's not necessary when you see that the arm comes undone, and blood flows out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it's crooked, should he stretch his arm hastily, for that would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it stay until he bleeds a second time, or you prick the tip of the flame with it, as long as the blood that has congealed comes out freely.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on 1 pot of silk soaked in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let him leave it alone and do not compress it, until the swelling has been reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed again from the blood a second time, you should let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for bleeding is that the sick person dips their hand into hot water until the scarlet-colored vein appears.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein is well seen, then let him bleed now from across, not from the length or the width.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the wound be wide and let him bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if there is no blood coming out, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood clot in the water, as long as you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's winter, don't put your hand back in hot water at all, for you would put it in colder than the warmth.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer than from all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the salivary gland of the right hand is worth to all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, so that you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the bleeding is across, and you cut off all of it completely, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too deep, for the nerves are under, entirely bare of flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood has congealed in the wound and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood flow as far as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do everything similarly to what I told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The sap of the soapwort is worth to all diseases that are under the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as illnesses of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the knees and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its sap is that the patients put their foot in hot water and rub on the sore part until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and tie above the joint of the foot; and the poultice is on the ankle, and above the foot they go out many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heal then the most swollen vein or at the ankle, which moves more worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves which are underneath, and the sap also works in a way as cutting; and the wound becomes useless.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the swelling cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let the poultice well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the sap fails the first time, then start it again the second time above a pot, because the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	don't be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and thus make from soapwort the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee of strength and its sap is worth for the pain of the loin when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its sap is that the patients enter into a bath and rub above the knee four turns while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and by passing through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth just as much as if you cut it, because the place is salty, and it is very swollen in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find the main vein, then heal any of its veins that are open behind the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do as much as you can to stop the bleeding, then loosen the bandage, and put on a compress of cotton and let it constrict; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	It looks like we've finished with the first section! Let's move on to the next one.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping which is done without piercing is done in two ways: either it's to be used hot, or not hot.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping which is done by piercing and the extraction of blood is done on 14 parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	for one is in the sole of the head and the others are in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on each side of the neck and the cupping under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cuppings on the two shoulders; and the cuppings above the buttocks.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cuppings in the two arms; and the cuppings in the two legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cuppings on the two ankles; and the cupping does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it has not weakened anyone much, as one would do with vein-stopping;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable that it be administered, neither hot nor cold, in any disease that comes from repletion, as long as the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of illnesses or by custom, we need to cup, let's administer it each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between each time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to cup, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such who find repletion and darkness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in themselves.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are bleeding.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such who dream, and see through the blood veins and wounds and deaths and seeming things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it's in the middle of the month, we will order to cup after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The vein-stopping of the nose helps in the inflammation of the head... that comes from within, and it is not suitable to be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this cupping takes the place of the vein-stopping of the temporal.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not suitable for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have a cathartic, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have or have had cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured by it often become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little further down to prevent forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping in the neck is in place of the vein-stopping of the head and of the temporal, and for this reason it is good for the constriction of the belly.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to rupture of the channel of the womb, and to swellings, and to repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be pressed a little, because if it holds too tightly, it will engender forgetfulness or obstruction of the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The cuppings on both sides of the neck are good for headaches, eye pains (obthalmia), and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the vein-stopping of the temporal. And you should command the healer to express his hand gently when applying it, so that he does not constrict the artery and draw out excessive blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cuppings under the chin are good for diseases of the mouth and corruption of the gums, and similar ailments that are in the mouth. And it takes the place of the vein-stopping on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cuppings under the armpits are good for diseases that come from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The cuppings of the sides (armpits) are as effective as those on three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and you should command the healer to not be too deep in his penetration, because the place is bare of fat and is next to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cup that is over the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath, and it needs to be large and made of copper, so that it can draw well. And perhaps if it were subtle, it would break through and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cups on the legs are obviously beneficial, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains in the hips, thighs, and bladder, and relieve swellings. And they take the place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankle veins. However, they weaken the body after long use and bring paleness to many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the cup is that you first put it on empty, and then seal it quickly, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and inflamed, and see the reddish color of the blood; then prick, and remove the cups, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick fat, and clear pores: in that case, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and slightly deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood a little at a time, we can suffice with just one [pricking].
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to draw out a lot of blood, we should prick often; and if the blood is thick, we should prick deeply, and the ends are such that the heart should be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the areas of the cups with oil that is appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's made from sweet almond oil or from the seed of a gourd.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's in vinegar, from oil of wormwood, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, you take bitter olive oil, or balsamic oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who is being cupped has tender flesh and large pores, then there should not be put any oil at all.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or hawthorn water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, should get up with ease, or with hawthorn water, and with sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or with water of scabies (a skin condition), or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to be cupped with a cup before the bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep afterwards.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary to be well-warmed, when one must be cupped and while being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are choleric (having a hot temperament), and whose blood is too agitated and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as unripe grapes and endives and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and melons, and kid (young goat) meat, and moistened meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup and medium-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and melons, and young chickens and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give certain men some tritacle or muscadine (a type of grape) before the cupping, or after, in order to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the blood should be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cups that are put without piercing (i.e. not drawing blood) are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gouty joints, and on the belly and navel and hips and thighs, because these members cannot bear to be pierced there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does not do this only in order to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the armpits when an abscess is forming; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just like when we put cups on the belly and navel to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain, when there is an abscess or ulcer; and perhaps by its attractive virtue it draws out the abscess, or dries up the ulcer in its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained fluid (edema).
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cups are administered empty in order to suck only, and sometimes they are administered with fire (heat), and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in the disease of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs that are suitable to this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup administered with fire is:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And let it be two thumbs' breadth in width and half a palm's depth, and let there be an incision around the middle one little porthole, as if to pierce with a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of lead so that when placed on the limb it does not hurt the patient.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle a rod of cross-wise iron or lead to place a candle within.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be great and small according to the sicknesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for children's cupping glasses are different from those of old people, and thin ones are different from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus must this cupping glass be placed over the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	light the candle with tallow or a wick, and place it in the cupping glass across from the rod that is inside the cupping glass,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping glass so it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and the thumbs should be over the porthole that we have said, so that when you want to, the steam goes out, and take off the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and then light the wick again just like before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass used for pleurisy, which is administered at every age, there is no rod nor porthole, and it is not administered unless it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	and that's its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	without cups are not administered unless to members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in naked places without skin, such as toes or heels, and other similar ones.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cups which are in sweet and clear water without sediment, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a new vessel with fresh sweet water until they have been soaked for a long time and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be purged with wine and cupping glasses, then rub the member so that it becomes red, and put on the cups.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and have drained, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it there, because it will be very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place from the cupping glass and then from the water, quite well, and then dry it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place has healed too late from the cups, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the cups are stopped.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the cup is multiplied, put on vitriol (a type of acid) dissolved or gallnuts and similar things, until it stops.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of peeled peas on the place and leave them until they burn against the place, it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other cups.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the stitches do not want to take hold, rub the fresh blood on the place, or insert a needle so that the stitches issue.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are loose, powder on a little aloes and linen thread, or ashes, so they will hold now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the treatment of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know well, dear son, that foolish men fall from this chapter, for they have never seen any of the old books, nor have they read any letters;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is estranged the knowledge in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except by the knowledge of the old books, or which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have written in this chapter what is contained, and I have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say the prologue of this book, the sum of speech and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on virtue, so that those who have experienced it know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any break or dislocation or twisting or sprain comes to a person, it is necessary for you to hasten to cure the sick from one side and, on the other hand, if no other thing is available, such as weakness of body, infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the temperature is not very hot or too cold; and I warn against chilled humors, that is to say, cold joints, and meat of fowl and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fat meats, and do not fill yourself too much with flesh foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of warm aposteme or spreading of matter in the member; so let the patient recover at my first governance which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore itself, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and cheese, and pigs, and beef, and fresh fish, and old wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with good nourishment the bone is repaired more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and those who are decrepit cannot be well repaired or mended according to their nature due to the scorching of the members, nor also those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, scrape over the broken bone, that is to say, great scabs that form and join the member together, as long as it strengthens itself again like before; and do not remove them immediately, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with thick meats, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that broken bones are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is another thing than the break of the rib or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that occur at the angle, and others in splintering, such as the break of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with an open wound, and a break with a small slit throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each kind has its own remedy, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory comes to.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the break of a bone occurs when the place is twisted and opens well from the outside, and sounds under the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or creaking, and the patient does not feel great pain, then it is not a break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or splitting, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But you must not move it with the hand, but rather put on medications that come later, and then straighten it out slowly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which occurs at the angle, and where the two parts are disjointed, you must now bring them back to an equal point, so that the swelling may come out.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and when the swelling comes, leave it alone for a day, until the swelling is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then bring it back to its proper position with the gentle and skilled use of a bandage, and know that the restoration of one piece is more light than the restoration of one with many parts. Then straighten it, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and you straighten two parts, whether it is an arm or leg, or on your hand if it is one small member, or with two strings, or with a string and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are reunited, you scrape away all the additions in their place with all sorts of bandages, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And be careful with it in your hand if you think it's not well done: straighten it properly, and don't pull or press too hard, as those who do so by their work bring about hot swelling and contraction to the member, as we have warned many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is properly set, then be sure to keep the patient still so that they do not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secure that the patient feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it does not feel any pain, then it is not yet in its proper position, and it must be put back into the right condition so that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure that it is put back in its proper place, so that twisting or crookedness does not occur when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: it is necessary to wrap them in fine and subtle linen cloth.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and sturdy linen cloth, for the large cloths enclose the entire large member and straighten it equally from all sides, so that there is no crease.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie the ends together with light stitches, three or four according to the member, and hold your hand on one end of the cloth, then go up above the break and tighten it less, so that the break is a little apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the cloth little by little, until you grasp a good part of the healthy place, then take another linen and turn it around again on top of the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and tighten it moderately, not too tight nor too loosely, as we said in the first layer above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the linen stitches some strips of linen or cloth, as long as they are all even, then tie everything up with one bandage, and then put your well-made straps on top, if there is no swelling or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is inflammation or swelling, then put something soothing on it, that calms the hot swelling and removes the inflammation, and leave it for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then tighten the straps up top, and they should be about half as wide as a well-made cane, or of the wood from which one makes calipers, or palm fronds, and should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it must be that the strap that you put on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should also be as long as it needs to be for the small or large member.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten the straps up top just like you did in the first layer, then tie above with a thread to bind them, just like in the first layer on the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the more tight it is above, the less; and it should be that the thread is moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of fine linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish men who make their stitches with cords of coarse linen twisted wrong, and that's a great mistake, for the stitch can't be even if it's too fine, and it shouldn't have more than a space of two fingers between each strap.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the points of the straps after being tightened in their healthy places, then put underneath them stitches of linen or torn cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the tendon is torn, I will say the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to bind all broken limbs with straps on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it's not necessary to put strong straps until after five days or seven, or more according to your caution against hot swelling.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and behold here the manner of ancient plasters to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is kept near the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundance of egg, and make this concoction neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. And this is the common way of plaster restoring a break in many ways, and especially for women and small children, because it's not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the break, dislocation, and torsion: take 3 parts of asphalt, 1 part of ladanum (a type of resin), 1 part of naphtha, 1 part of gum arabic, 10 parts of musk, 5 parts of myrrh, 14 parts of aloes, 8 parts of alchemil (a type of root), and grind them into powder. Then mix them with abundance of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is worth for torsion: take musk and vaseline, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 9 parts; aconite, 6 parts; Armenian balm, 10 parts, and grind them well. Then mix with vinegar or abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of plaster for joints and broken bones that are out of their place, and it relieves the pain accompanying them, and is used to cut off the use of the bone and break: take new linen, moisten it in olive oil and let it cool, and put it on the spot. This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot swelling and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that heals broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and earth leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone break and to reduce the remaining swelling: take roots of camomile, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and grind them, then mix with wine. And if the member is warm, mix it with moist coriander water or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of plaster that is stronger than the first one, when hard swelling comes to restore the member: take roots of camomile, and seeds of flax, balsam, melilotus, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind them, then mix with salt water or sweet water or with wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that for a broken member to be restored well, one should not put anything on it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two [i.e., neither too soft nor too hard].
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to agree that for a broken member to be restored, one should put on it dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is worth for lesion and pain: take musk and hairs from depilated men or feathers from birds, and equal amounts, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen the plaster a little after, and be careful if the patient feels any pain or if the bone has not returned to its place, do not remove the plaster for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place or itching, redness, or swelling, hasten and remove it, and take away the plaster now; and take light cloth and a moist sponge of the sea, and plunge them in water, and lift up the place until the itching ceases and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen that has been moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it up with a knot, until you are sure there is no hot swelling.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and may the pain be removed, then start again with a subtle stitch and a little plaster, and do not bind it too tightly as before, and make them fine until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have completely disappeared, and you need to use plaster and bandages again, then repeat it, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of what we have said happens to the member, then do not remove it for three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes let it be twenty days, according to what is seen, until the break is set and approaches the joining of the flesh together.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then the constriction is more than before, and the flesh thickens, as I said before. And if you see that the place dries out more than is necessary, know that putrefaction will not come to it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then wash the place with hot water daily, and each time you remove it, and let it dry a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	by this work the corruption is cut off from the member, and it heals quickly, unlike what foolish men do, who restore the broken member wrongly: that's bad, and it's a cowardly act, and I see nothing but shame in doing it incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Les différentes manières de brisure qui ont été décrites sont :
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and various forms, and their causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breaks that are caused by the percussion of a sword, and the elbow breaks all the bone just up to the splinter which is under the bone, as done with an axe or a club; and because of this it is called this manner of break "haiche".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of break "absolute"; and the wounds of these two breaks are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a crushing blow, or splitting, or from the fist of stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a bursting break, which approaches just to the cloth that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is closed in the bone as subtle as a thread, and it is the small splitting, and because of this it is called this break "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound that is made by being struck with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to go inwards, and it is the hole that is charred like when blacksmiths heat up their forges; if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have soft bones in the skull, such as the skulls of infants.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and this happens with all these kinds of breaks where small pieces are pulled out, just like that; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the kinds of breaks by their signs above them, and by the examination that has been done, and by the foul matter that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary sign is known by this: when the bone has been uncovered and one rubs it in with their fingers, if the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the bad symptoms of the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, paleness, fever, or their pulse to be fast and red, and other similar signs in different conditions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening accident and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first and it's in winter, then it is convenient to take out the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to take out the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents that we have said come.
