Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone comes just to the flesh that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the broken part thus: and so take hold of the patient's head wounded, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound as soft as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the bleeding of blood comes out to uncover the bone, or an abscess hot, then take care with what is necessary, and so fill in the place with moistened cloth steeped in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest as long as the hot abscess is calmed down and you are sure that the bleeding has stopped; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut with a narrow chisel in front, and here's the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another chisel larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a variety of chisels, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of hard iron; and work lightly, so that you don't harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, then it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can insert chisels with handles, but not too deeply that they perforate through to the test of the skull, and on top of the point should be a margin or a circle, that doesn't let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one goes in its place of the depth of the bone, so that you have handles for all sides; and this is the shape of the three ways of handles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one handle on top of the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone is pierced; then move the handle to another place a little later, and do all around in this way; then cut with the nippers the space of the bone that is between the piers, and do so more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you bring out the bone into your hand, or onto any of the tools that you have such as tongs, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, then it is necessary that you resaw the remainder of the bone to all one another instrument similar to a nippers, but it should be more sharp and more subtle than the other nippers.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if any small bones or scales remain, then remove them lightly with one of the instruments; and then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working that Galen says is more sure, and he praises it highly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the break is visible; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will put underneath the head of this incisive lens something of which it is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and it is the part sharp in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet on top, so that you lightly chip the bone all around, and be well guarded of the thread that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, then chip it lightly, because one chips well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate all the way to the thread, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small pieces, then cover up that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp of which you should have various quantities, so as to make it most convenient at each place according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass in front of coarse rasps, and then of finer ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and subtle breaks, you should make adjustments according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily mastered by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scar is exposed, it is advisable that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the scar;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled cloth in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so that you don't hurt the scar, then apply another string on top, but not pull it tight until it just reaches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it so for one day or two, until the abscess has calmed down, then remove the string and apply medicines such as lily roots, flour of vetches, powder of incense, artemisia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and apply it to the wound, and continuously administer medicinal remedies without applying any kind of bite or mordification.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and be careful that the wound is thoroughly clean, so that you don't leave any grease or allow it to form a scab, for when the scab forms over the tissue of the brain, it will cause them to rot and burst, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something biting is applied to the scar, it becomes inflamed on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, for if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is no blackening over the wound that goes beyond what the medicine on it has caused, which is due to its virtue, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them with one cloth, and apply it to the scar.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him in the manners of treatments that are required, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that at no time are the two parts of the nose above or one below alone broken, for they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is crushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is advisable that you set your little finger or thumb of the nose, and put this fracture into your index finger, and into the pouch behind, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part of the nose above, and cannot be brought to its place by the finger, it is advisable that you put a small piece of cloth or a bandage on top of the wound, so that it can hold it steady.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in both parts, do the same again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if not on the first day, then after seven or ten days, when the swelling has calmed down, then bind a cloth of linen around the nose's tip, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another cloth on the other part, if it is broken there; and let the folds be so big that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that you should moisten the folds with marrow and change them each day. It doesn't seem to me that this is good, but it's advisable that they be moistened in the making of egg bread dough and mill powder; then let the cloth remain until the bone is hardened and the cartilage is stiffened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes bind on or to the nose a pair of goose's quills in place of cloths, and if you have a soft drape around them, and it holds the fracture together, and makes a gentle breeze for the patient to breathe through; then do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerot or cotton moistened in rose oil or a little flask of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if swelling doesn't come, put an ointment on the back of it from flour of saponaria and incense powder, mixed with egg bread dough, then apply light compresses and don't bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nose's fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, you should extract them with suitable instruments, then sew up the wound, and treat it with things that bring nourishment to flesh and uniting, such as poultices and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, you should treat it with bandages and put linseed oil compresses on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems like we've switched to a new topic.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath, and there is no wound outside, and the break is outside alone, and it is not cracked in two, but rather split open inside, then one recognizes this easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you push your left index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left jawbone, then push your left index finger from the right hand, and gently push the break inside, and secure it with the other hand from outside, and tie equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split into two, then it is necessary that you administer extension of 1/4 parts [of the jaw] so long as it be equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the dislocation of the teeth has caused movement or wounding, then strain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw gum, and place on the gum one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made estelle, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it on with a knot that you can see, and command the patient to rest, and serve light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's face is changing, then take off the splint on the third day, and then put back together what was changed; and apply a poultice on top, with flour mixed with egg or linseed meal powder, after you have removed the gum; and put on a light linen cloth, and if the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as is until they are healed; many times people heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times [i.e., the poultice and rest].
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, remove no part of the bone that is loosened; be careful to extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it by flaying according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all of these pieces and none remains, the wound, if it is wide, should be covered with one of the ointments that are prescribed for this purpose to draw out blood, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of great violence
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture is broken multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and has fragments, and this is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without an open wound, you should have two assistants, so that one can hold the splint which feels the fractured part, and the other extend the arm towards the part; then place the break even with your hands, so that the shape be as it should be, and there be no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded pole of cloth or linen, and it should be thick according to your necessity; then stretch and lift the splint, and press the pole with your hand, so that you place even the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the splint forward because it goes too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies on their side and places under their shoulder a medium-sized pillow, and have the assistants press the shoulder downward, so that the bone of the splintered part is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the break with your hands, and if you find that it is not properly aligned, it is necessary to split it slightly, and pull out the lighter fragments, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, you should cut at one of the instruments that you have; but place under the splinter this instrument, in order to protect the flesh.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And shape it like a spoon, and it should not be crooked, and it should be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two handles, just like you see, and one wide and the other narrow, just like the incision that you made when you cut the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that the wound is well-aput (i.e. has formed a scab), then clean the wound, and if the incision is small or you doubt whether it has formed a scab, then cover the wound with linen and gauze, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms there, it is moistened with a cloth dipped in olive oil, rose oil, and vinegar, and applied.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The splinting of the bone, when it is from wounds and cuts, is that you place the splint on a cloth made of flour meal powder and egg white, and put light bandages over it, and put a spear under the splint, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very long bandage of one palm in width, then place a double cloth over the bandages and splint; then take a thin strip of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandaged part, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the strip over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the healthy neck, and under the sound hip, and under the sick hip; and loosen each part of it, and when you see that the dressing holds the bone together well, and you see clearly that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then reward each day, and when the ligaments relax, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and have the sick person sit with his arms behind his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under his hip to lift the injured area upwards; this will alleviate the fracture by aligning the shoulder joint, or by binding the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the splint if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it on until he is restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and in less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Il semble que nous avons fini cette transcription d'un texte médical ancien, peut-être du Moyen Âge.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder blade is broken or its place becomes too large and cannot be contained; and it does not seem to be healed by touch alone; if it appears according to the shape of the breakage, and it is reset in accordance with its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put powder from the mill on the joint along with an abundance of egg white, and lightweight bandages, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide and thin strip above the shoulder, about one digit larger than the shoulder, and sew ribbons under the strip at any point on the shoulder so that the hair of the linen bandages is evenly woven in with them; and then hold it fast with a strong bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and check the knot every day; and each time you notice looseness, retighten it, and put even the strip if it has moved out of its place, and have the patient rest on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number is completed, release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that becomes loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points under the skin, take it out and cauterize it, and do what we have said to alleviate the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet ! La "brisure du pis" se réfère probablement à une blessure ou une fracture du sein (le terme "pis" est ancien et désigne le sein).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens infrequently; however, it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken inside, it leans towards the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, a lack of sensation, and numbness, and by chance, vomits blood, and the sinews appear in the fractured bone, and he senses everything badly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join together the ribs of the two rib bones with their hands, and subtly try to put it in every way you can, so that the shape of the bone be as it should; then place poultices and bandages above the sterile linen of salt or another light wood, and wrap it up in one cloth, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and turn the cord around to the back, and bind it tightly, and reward each hour with ease, and if it swells, then tighten it; and if it is necessary to untie it, because of corrosion or itchiness that comes to the place, or pain or inflammation, then hasten, and untie it, and scrape off the poultice, and address what has come out in ways of cures; then wash away the poultice, and bind it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons une section de texte médical du Moyen Âge traitant de la fracture des côtes. Les deux passages que vous avez mentionnés semblent être extraits d'un même texte.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in their large places behind the back, and inside the head, and do not protrude except because they are slippery; and everyone feels it well at the examination of the bones.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put back the break, just as it should be. And then apply the plaster and a bandage made of steel, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is inclined inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncture, just like from a stab wound, because the bone pierces the flesh; and swells with red spots, and burns and vomits a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the old doctors have used great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do so, lest hot pustules arise there, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And one of us said that you put cupping glasses on the place, to suck out the matter, and this seems like reason; nonetheless, there is doubt whether the cupping glass will attract impurities to the place because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one of us said that the place should be covered with moist linen in hot oil, and tents should be placed between the ribs to put the hurt place equal all around; then it should be treated with the treatment of a stab wound, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient's mind, it seems necessary to cut open above the broken rib, and it is necessary to put a device underneath to keep the spleen safe; and then one must saw through the bone, and pull out gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is cured. de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bone of the neck, and it bends; and also to the spine of the back.

And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, it doesn't hurt. de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken scrotum
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the scrotum are broken many times, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration is that you tie two strings, one above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches each member to his part equally; and that is when the breakage is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient. And also if it is close to the thigh, and then place the strings near the thigh, and stretch downwards; then put the splint on the bones equally with his two hands, so that it will according to its natural shape, and then put a compress on it, and tie it, if there are swellings, they will not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it cool down then return to your task and treatment; the tie is done in this manner.

Then place a pad on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and scrotum with soft cloth to even out the constriction. Then begin to tie tightly 3 or 4 turns around the breakage; and as you go up from the breakage, loosen the tension. Then take hold of the two ends of thread that you inserted between the leg and scrotum, and tie 3 pads above them; then return to the bottom end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and if it does not move from its place, leave it so; for if there is no swelling, or inflammation, or other similar sign, do nothing more.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a problem, then untie and adjust what has happened, as we have said many times before. And if there are pieces of bone that protrude, it is necessary to remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area and pull out the splintered bone; and treat it as we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at any time the shin is broken in such a way that stars are put on it, as in the arm and the shoulder; nonetheless, in this restoration made, the patient does not sound.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the shin is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little breakage, but it folds many times. And if it breaks, it is only by a split, or i.e. a hole, and it has to be sewn up with much pain, and without pain, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put back what was broken to its place, as much as it can be assembled so that you can move it; then put the plaster on, and I put a round splint on it, if you need one, and strain it as it should be, then repair all the preparations that we have said in other breaks, such as applying heat and another appearance; then put on each accident what is fitting for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by name "ulna" (or "mustelz") and the other is called "fibula" (or "foscile"); and it has all other breakages as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides. (i.e. it's a compound fracture)
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then turn the front side. (i.e. the fibula, which is a thinner and more delicate bone)
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the thick bone is broken, then one feels great pain and it can be seen well; and turn to underneath. Then make an extension, and put it back in place, and tie the splints equally; but nonetheless, it is fitting that if the break is ugly, and there are several pieces, that the extension should be smaller and lighter; and dress according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have completed your work, take two pieces of wooden splint that extend from one part of the leg to the other and are as long as the leg from the knee down. Then wrap them in two loops one on top and the other below, and tie them securely in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and it will be well done. Some people give a single piece of wood as long as the leg, and place it under the leg to prevent movement, and this is properly done in the break where there is a wound; and each day move the leg to see if there is an abscess or other accident. If you treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bone of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes the bones of the foot do break and are shattered, and you must be cautious, for there can be a great deal more damage.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot are broken and you see them overlapping each other, then lay such sick person on the ground, as if it were going to walk, and then place his foot upon the other one where the bones are raised, and press down upon them until they return to their proper place; then apply a dressing and bandage over it, and place under the foot of the injured person a small wooden splint with two hooks on it, and bind it securely to the foot properly; then wrap up the foot in a cloth and do other things as you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, untie the splint, for you will find that the bones are aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand. Then place on each broken toe a splint according to its length and somewhat thicker, then put under the foot that wooden splint I mentioned and bind it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, place on each one a splint according to their quantity wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind them with the splint under the foot; and let it be so that the end of the splint sticks out from under the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, just as we have discussed them; and treat each case according to what is proper.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the wrist.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, cause her to sit and be enlarged, then bend her towards the part of the back, and have her held from behind; then fill the natural hole with cotton, and put as big a stone in it as .i. fist; then let down the woman, and lift up the back little by little, and then the cotton will jump out until it reaches the entrance of nature, and the bone will return to its place with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in and do this for .vij. days or around that: if it will be restored the breakage, and you see, take a bladder of heather, and tie a cord to the anus of an animal, and insert the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the cord strongly until the bladder is blown out inside: nature will return the breakage; then fill with cotton and leave it so for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the elbow or man is broken, or that of a woman, so restore it in such a way as we have said for the hipbone; and these recent breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and skill into them and listens to my book. For the break signifies the right path of restoration in several dispositions; listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap cloth around it and let it be for 3 days or so: it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is severe, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated now, so that the treatments we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and it remains with vitriol, if you have nothing else to do, then start again to reset the fracture in the same hour or that day, lest an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes there, let the resetting alone until the ninth day, so long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third nor on the fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin's surface, it is necessary that you set it at a light angle with your hands, to slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you don't have the extension handy to set it at an angle with your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the doctor to take three or four of these, as needed in each treatment of a fracture; and let them be round and a large pock, so they don't bend when compressed on the member you're working on, and let them have a groove ahead, and be thick in the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved fingers should be placed on top of the visible bone; and press down once, so that it returns, and let them be equal to each other. And if the fracture is fine, and the instruments cannot take hold of the bone well, then you must cut off the end of the bone, so that the instrument can have a grip on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, take a suitable tool, such as an awl or saw, at your disposal; then scrape out what remains in the bone from sharpness and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned to its place and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural location. Do so much that it is in its place, then moisten one cloth in black vinegar and properly apply it; and do not put cerote or anything oily on the wound lest it bring forth infection and corruption; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times the foolish physician has done this, and brought death or decay upon the patient sometimes; and the bandages should be softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that evil occurrences will arise from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the location, then do not put salves on it; but wrap it tightly around with hard cloths, and bind them. And when you see after one day or two that the bowstring is beginning to form at the wound, then remove what you have put on top with vinegar, and apply ointment for healing wounds, such as tetraformulated ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dress the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be arranged in such a way that the bowstring hangs downwards lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for many days and cannot heal but instead forms a bowstring, know that there are small bones inside, which is why it is necessary to clean the wound with tent (possibly referring to a medical instrument or technique) and remove all these loose pieces of bone that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or other manner of corruption comes to the place, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and appears on the member, such as the bones of the shin or the hip, and similar ones of the large members, do not remove it, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Bruises come many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps the member cannot do its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the bruise is fresh: if you administer stringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe juice, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with strong vinegar or with egg white or with oil; and apply it to the bruise in compresses, and bind it well, and do not remove it for a day; and then unbind it, and begin another one, as long as the swelling is gone; or you tie on a piece of cloth that has been well made; for the property of cloth is that it removes all the swellings from the members; and if the bruise has already become hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then scrape it off with a scraper, so that its superfluity becomes apparent; or you have it taken out by a barber, as long as it is gone, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is healed, and after the member remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ties, and the swelling could not come to the member; or due to a multitude of hemorrhages; or due to too great movements, nor in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well and make their body soft, until the blood is multiplied in them; and give them baths, and give them joy and comfort; then apply poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts to it a great swelling, and brings forth a bloody discharge, as long as the swelling comes to the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the member is ugly, although it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one must break the entire limb anew, and many foolish healers have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great evils, and perhaps even death. However, if the swelling and pain are fresh, then they should be drained with hot water or cooked herbs that soothe, such as mulberry leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a soothing plaster, such as a well-made diachylon, and take the juice of mulberry leaves, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on it. Or take ripe figs, and grind them with coltsfoot flaxseed, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at any time the swelling is removed through continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands, and gentle movements should be made to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting has become hardened and stiff, like stone, and needs to be removed with an iron instrument, then it should be carefully cut just up to the bone, with a fine, light incision. And apply a cautery and styptic powder in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by a joint moving out of its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to any joint, it should now be reset to its original place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Because if you wait, the joint becomes swollen, and by chance if it is reset in pain, then you should not move it to its original place until it has ceased to be swollen: many times it comes to have spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Anyway, when this happens, you should make the patient rest, then let him be until the swelling has gone down; then warm up the limb with hot water and oil, then gently rub it clean, and cure each member as the doctor will come to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocation from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Something happens when the jaws are dislocated and they hang down, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are a little pulled out of their place and become a little soft; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva from the mouth drips that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its proper place by itself in a short while.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully dislocated, you should gently rub it, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in this way that the minister will hold the patient's head and insert the mirror with a small pouch from one of his hands into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if it is on both sides; and with the other two hands be outside to put everything back in its place; and order the patient to open and close his jaws and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror is placed in its correct position until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is not easy to return, that is, if it are the two jaws together, then warm them up with hot water and oil, until they can be gently rubbed in; do not delay the return, as we said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned to their proper position and the patient's mouth closes well without swelling, then put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil and wax, and tie them gently with soft strings.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back and his legs are between two cushions, so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor does he try to move, but rather takes soft food until the pains are gone and the jaws are numb.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he should eat lightly what he wants and not force himself to open his mouth while eating or drinking, as long as the jaws are numb and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be restored to their proper place within an hour and are not returned to their place, it leads to fever and sharp pain, and perhaps colic and maybe vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these things, then know that it is a disaster; and often, in eight days, death comes to the person who has it.
de la forcelle	(dislocation of the jaw)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation of the jaw cannot be released from its original position inside the face and behind the earlobe, and is released only once on the outside, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then he presses firmly on the dislocated point with your palm, and it will return to its place; then put on a poultice and bandage it in place.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the leg which is on the outside cannot be dislocated; if it is not so, and if it does happen to dislocate once, then rub it gently back into place, as we said earlier; then put on a poultice and bandage it in place, and order the patient to rest until they are fully healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly is returned the leg of the hip when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	It is known that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the lower part of the arm bone; and the second is at the upper part of the shoulder blade; and perhaps it dislocates at the top, and this rarely happens.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and it dislocates downward toward the arm bone many times, especially in those who have little flesh, for then it slips out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out slowly, and comes back slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that there is a blow or crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot tumor, and they think it has been dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must then examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And a skilled person knows when it is a dislocation downward toward the arm bone, and he makes a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them obvious differences.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and under the arm bone a lump, just like an egg; and the sick one cannot bring his hand to his chest, nor move it with any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it clearly at the shoulder.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not to be reduced when it is new or if the child has an illness.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the servant lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts his fingers under the arm bone, and lifts the joint with force to its place; and the servant lifts the hand and stretches it out high, then puts it back in. It will come together quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come together as we have said in a day or two, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water; and the servant should bring him soothing and calming substances, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and mallalote in water, and bring them to him.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then have the patient sit on their back, and put a woolen pad, not too soft nor too hard, under the arm bone. Then have the servant place their heel on top of the pad, and gently lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another servant should tie the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward. In this way, the shoulder will return to its place immediately, and if you see that it is still swollen according to this method...
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you make someone, i.e. a person who is bigger than the patient, be present, and stand straight next to them, and press their shoulder under the arm bone of the patient, and lift the arm bone up high, so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another servant should pull the patient's hand downward towards their stomach. And if the patient is too light, they can be helped to hold something heavy, and then the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the patient is also healed in another way: and it is that you stick a long iron rod into the ground, with the end of which is as thick as a fist, and not too big or too small...
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it should be placed under the patient, so that it is covered with a soft cloth on top, and the patient's hand should extend down from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return despite all the things we have said, make this treatment: take a rod of two arm-lengths and four finger-widths in diameter, with one end sharp enough to easily enter deep under the arm bone, in this shape...
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth on the top of the rod so that the rod does not hurt the patient, and place it under the arm bone of the patient. Then stretch your arm over the long rod and tie the assistant's hand to the rod at the head of the hand, then place the arm on a splint of one wooden board width thick, and let the hands hang down and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that you place under the arm bone a wooden splint of equal thickness, then put the bandage around with miller's powder, incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then stretch it under the arm bone gently, and turn the strap on top of the bandage, and hold the hand against your neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that you check on the patient frequently, until the limbs are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then check again after five or seven days, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from its normal place because of dampness or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauterizers to three small holes, as one would do before a cauterizer's procedure.
