Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things and it comes apart after seven days, and the joint does not hold together, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut, stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs in the chest area, shoulders, or back is caused by a blow or a stretch of the limbs, and another treatment is administered to it; and the treatment continues until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes inflammation and slowness in the movement of the member, then have the patient bathe many times, until that inflammation is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the elbow joint.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to those points; and it has been dislocated from all sides, as well as in front of and behind, and the dislocation cannot be restored because it can be seen and felt clearly; and dislocation occurs according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the diseased shoulder with the healthy one, it can be seen clearly. Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its own shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to cleanse it immediately, before the pus comes, because if the pus were to come, it would be grievous to remove it; and perhaps cannot be removed entirely, especially when it is in the back; it is worth less than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death will come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this when it can be reduced, that you stretch out his hand with your two hands; and his arm should be spread out, and the fingers of the doctor according to the shoulder around, above and below, and push the joint into its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand into his other hand, and pushes the shoulder which is dislocated from the root of his palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to come back to its place, administer strong extension; and have two people extend the arm, and hold it with both hands, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then wrap a long and wide double cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the doctor has joined the joint to his hand, he sprinkles some oil on it to loosen the joint, then pushes the joint firmly, until it comes back.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is back in place, he puts on dry plaster with plenty of egg, and wraps the arm firmly, and lets the patient's arm rest for a while, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is strong and in its place, he releases the bandage and lets it be; and if you see that the joint does not heal well, he repeats the plaster and the bandage, and lets it rest for a while, until it is firmly set, then he releases it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels great pain after the reduction of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, he bathes and rubs it gently, and presses until it is relieved; or he puts a thick sheep's wool poultice on the joint, then lets it be for one day and one night, then removes it and makes him enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, he rubs the joint gently, then puts the poultice back on, and then makes him enter the bath; and thus does it two or three times until he is healed; and if you see that, he puts on warm, moistened linseed flax with butter, and wraps it around; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	Il semble que nous sommes revenus à la question initiale !
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return to its place is light, lighter than other joints Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place immediately, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the place remains swollen, or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is such that you place the ailing hand on a table, and stretch out the members of the hand, and have the physician put it equally, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the jointure, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Nevertheless, you must see if it is well in place; then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then have the patient put the back of his hand on the table, and the physician put his hand over that appearance of the jointure. If it returns now, it's well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain on emollient poultices to cool the abscess, and let it be like that without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you can't put it in place after any days, then the twisted joint will remain.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and nothing harms the patient more than for his hand to remain swollen and unable to grasp anything: then know that the nerves are crushed or the arteries; if there is no other cause worse than to strain by cauterizing near the case, and it may be that this is not worth anything.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then strain and leave it for 5 days, then release and let it be like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well and there is any swelling, then soak the hand in hot water and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Dislocation of the wrist (or forearm). It seems like we've been reading a medieval medical text on how to treat this condition!
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At times the forearm is dislocated in either direction, sometimes towards the back of the palm or into the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then the forearm will be in its place, and push the dislocation back into its socket as far as it returns. Then support the head of the forearm, and move it towards the part where it was disjointed.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it be for 2 days, and then put it back in its place that same day. And from then on bind it as we have said, and release the bandage every night, and make it move, and rebind it tightly; and do this often, until it becomes strong again.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do exactly the same thing if it is dislocated towards the palm of the hand, and do so just as you have done here before, until it is healed; and do exactly the same thing when it is dislocated in any other way.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the spine (vertebrae) of the back. Another potentially serious medical condition!
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or if there are more than one that are dislocated, there is no cure, for the bone quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excretions jump out without any will, and he cannot hold them, and many times they are loosened in some member, or both thighs, or the two arms, or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the vertebrae move in four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gyphosis".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	the cure is that you reward him if the gyphosis came from childhood: then there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old-fashioned methods of cures were to use great words, and it was not a great benefit in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the kyphosis (or hunchback) that comes at the front of the chest, there is no cure nor healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight to the sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which properly comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be stretched out on his back in one position equally, and have a poultice (or strain) under him so that he does not get hurt.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then place a heated iron at his head on the ground firmly, and another at his feet, and bind a strip of cloth over the joints of the patient, and one to his hips, legs, knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two attendants know how to bind the strips of cloth, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two heated irons.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be well closed, the iron as we have said, and the attendant places his hands on the patient's spine firmly, until it returns to its normal position.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three arms length in width, and sharpen the edge on one side, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board on the back's skin, then put the middle part of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and have the attendant place their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its proper position; and if you see fit, do the same treatment to the vertebra that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And have two heated irons placed at the head of the patient, one arm's length apart, and towards his feet another two, with a hand's breadth between each iron, above and below.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each iron a hole, or the vertebra is pierced, and let the irons be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of irons there should be another turning iron, on which the bandages turn, and on each turning iron there are two small irons an inch long, to turn the vertebra.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then bind the bandage that is between the joints to the turning iron near the head, and the other bandage to the other turning iron towards the feet; and each of the attendants turns their turning iron with all the bandage, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is straight, he puts on a drying poultice with abundance of egg, and then the compresses, and then an ointment from a tablet three fingers long, which will bring the place of the kyphosis and the healthy part of the spine to health, then binds it with a bandage, as we have said, and uses the patient in gentle nourishment until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if no cure comes in the end of healing, it is suitable to administer softening and soothing medicines with the ointment that we have said before; and never give one piece of alum,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and if the appearance comes in the rear part of the spine of the back, and take it for dislocation; and that is the bone that opens up, so one must not have any presumption about it: perhaps death would result.
des dislocations de la hainche	The Dislocations of the Hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder are prone to dislocations alone, and it is not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is displaced in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inwardly towards the contrary side, and somewhat displaced in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the sick knee joint opens more than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in front.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place where there are swellings of hot abscess, because the tendons of the thigh come to that place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one whose dislocation is in the back is that this accident is contrary to those in the front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one whose dislocation is in the front are that they bend their leg well according to its completion; however, they do not double their knee with pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and retain their urine, and swell the ankle, and when they go, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one whose dislocation is in the back are that they cannot straighten their knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the tendons of the thigh are at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this condition of dislocation are that you return to see if the dislocation is ancient, and it remains in its position, then there is no cure; and one must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of three manners of dislocation, then hurry to turn the joint inward and outward, and move it from right to left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must have a strong assistant appear, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with one bandage that is bound over the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another attendant stretches their hand up in such a way that they press their hands under the patient's buttocks, then tightens it with a strong bandage over the thigh; and another one ties the end of the bandage.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and stretch it upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground for an instant, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to all three appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If it is not so, then you must apply a cure to its appearance. When the dislocation is in the part behind, then you must bind the patient on their healthy side, then place the bandage over the root of the thigh, and the place under the ankle, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the ankle, and towards the muscle.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another attendant's arms and encircle the thick part of the sick thigh, and stretch it out to the back firmly: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot bind it in this manner that we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage soft on the two heels and on the two knees, and let the sick leg be stretched two fingers longer than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then let it be hung up on the head of a beam, and let it be suspended above the ground two arms' length; then command one attendant to encircle the head of the thigh, and have another attendant hang with the patient, who encircles firmly the thigh, because the joint returns now hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in the back, then let the patient lie on their side, as we have said in the one with kyphosis, and stretch a bandage over the sick leg properly, and over the pubic bone as well.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two irons, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one iron between the thighs of the patient in the middle.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have damp cloths wrapped around it so that the patient is not hurt, then have each attendant stretch towards them and the physician puts their hand on the dislocation to guide them.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, put them on the table and press them as we have said in kyphosis, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick leg hastily and as I have said; and the physician should place their hand over the painful ankle, then press with the other hand and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards or lift them up onto their feet, but rather they should be positioned as if the hip were displaced backwards, as we have said in the bed with two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on their back, and the bandage stretched as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be in place when the patient stretches out their legs and they are equal; then align the thighs, apply a poultice, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient rests for three or four days, then you remove the bandage and apply a poultice on top of it; and if you see that they are equal, then you bind them as before, and leave it so for three days, then remove it and let the patient walk slowly until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	The Dislocation of the Knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee joint is displaced in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not get displaced forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg to their thigh, and if it does not straighten out to its normal position, know that it is displaced.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit up straight, and stretch out their leg if they can, and place your back on their chest, and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee in your hands and pull it back between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee joint firmly; and have another attendant stretch out their foot until the knee joint returns to its place, and the sign is that they straighten out their leg easily.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and apply the poultice on top of it, and have them stretch out their leg to their thigh, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then release them; and do not let the patient walk again until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the members are not in place, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	The Dislocation of the Ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the calf is swollen, and tends to turn towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the remedy is light, and one should stretch it lightly with their hands when it is only sprained.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, then you must have the patient sit up straight and have one attendant stretch out their foot over the ankle from above.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot in your right hand and then in your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards and press firmly the foot up.
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, then start again with the work, because it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground and insert a wooden bar firmly into the earth between their thighs, and wrap cloths around to prevent them from being hurt.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have the attendant tie the thigh, and another attendant stretch out the foot to their hands or with one bandage, so that it is tied around the ankle's collar.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch both attendants equally, and the bar be placed between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when they are being stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the physician guide their hands to the dislocation, and another attendant ties the healthy leg below it, and the dislocation will return hastily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, then apply the poultice and bandages on top, and bind them firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the bandage is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then let it be for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, bind again; then release it on the third or fourth day, and have the patient rest and not walk for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before this time is up, it's not certain that he won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then you must alleviate them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	The Wrist
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the wrist is dislocated, it should be stretched carefully without great effort, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, then you must have the patient sit on a flat stone or on a table right up straight, and place their foot on what is visible of the joint, then press with their own foot firmly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is equal and there is nothing visible, then place under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then stretch firmly and leave for three days, then release; and have the patient rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Wounds and Dislocations Together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times there will be that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and slow to act, nor too hasty;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use soothing remedies first, a warm poultice, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then remove the dislocation now so that the warm poultice comes to the place.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies and warm poultices, and cure the wound if it seems fitting, with drying ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a break with the dislocation and small bones are shattered, then set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arm and body's safety. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the treatise on surgery.
